Tianjin: Li Tingyu Concurrently Serves as Chairman of the Southern Canal Dredging Committee 72

The lower reaches of the Southern Canal in Hebei Province have been silted up for many years. In order to facilitate transportation, the Southern Canal Lower Reaches Dredging Committee was specially established, with Li Tingyu, a member of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, concurrently serving as the chairman. The secretariat is headed by Yang Dianyuan, who also serves as the head of the General Affairs Section. The section is divided into three divisions: accounting, general affairs, and documentation, as well as investigators, surveyors, chief supervisors, and supervisors. In addition, there is an Engineering Department headed by a director and deputy director, who oversee five section chiefs, civil engineers, and a general affairs director. As for the dredging project, it starts from Jiuxuan Dam in Jinghai and ends at Jingang Bridge in Tianjin, totaling over 160 li. The cost is tentatively set at 300,000 yuan. The entire project is scheduled to be completed by the end of June. The committee has already started working in Nansha Street, Tianjin, and is intensifying its work.

Peking University Holds "May Fourth" 17th Anniversary Commemoration Meeting - Special Dispatch from Peiping 73

Meeting Held in a Peaceful Manner

May is a month of many events, especially in this eventful Peiping. Therefore, at 3:00 PM on April 30th, Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Jiyan convened a temporary security meeting and decided that all police and security teams in the city would suspend their days off on "May 1st" Labor Day, stepping up precautions against petty criminals taking the opportunity to cause trouble. Sure enough, that day passed peacefully. The following day was the anniversary of the "May 3rd" tragedy, and fortunately, there were no unexpected incidents. Next came the 17th anniversary of the "May Fourth" Movement.

Several days beforehand, news spread that any commemorative meeting would not be allowed. Even "Peking University," which at the time served as the main base, and subsequently added it specially to the school calendar each year, granting a day off different from other schools, according to school authorities, would temporarily cancel this day off this year. Therefore, on the afternoon of the 2nd, representatives from various classes at Peking University met in the reception room of the school's Fourth Dormitory and resolved to hold the commemorative ceremony as usual in a so-called "peaceful manner." The so-called "peaceful manner" contained three points: absolute adherence to a peaceful attitude, absolute abstention from strikes and demonstrations, and limitation to holding commemorative meetings and issuing commemorative declarations. Under these conditions, they obtained the consent of the school authorities to hold the commemorative meeting and also obtained permission from the local authorities to hold the commemorative meeting. Other schools did likewise.

Secret Police Swarming Inside and Outside the Venue

As the "May Fourth" Commemoration Day arrived, this reporter made a special trip to Peking University that morning to see what was happening. First, I went to the school's Third Courtyard, where I saw dozens of soldiers and police officers densely stationed in front of the antique gate and walls, along with more than a dozen plainclothes detectives. Next, I went to the school's First Courtyard. Here, in front of the Red Building, there were about twice as many soldiers, police, and plainclothes detectives as in the Third Courtyard, and the security was even tighter. Entry and exit were completely prohibited. Finally, I arrived at the school's Second Courtyard, the location of the commemorative meeting. In front of the gate and walls here, there was a large row of motorcycle police, two or three dozen in all, all carrying box cannons, facing west, and thirty or forty military police, divided into three or four layers, facing east, paying special attention to entering and exiting students.

The lotus pond area in front of the auditorium was heavily guarded by police, giving the impression of a sentry every five steps and a post every ten steps. Plainclothes detectives moved back and forth like shuttles, numbering over twenty or thirty in total. Whenever two or three people stood together talking, these detectives would definitely come over to stand and listen intently or deliberately run back and forth among the people, forcing them to disperse. When this reporter entered the auditorium, I saw several detectives in black hats on the podium, loudly reciting couplets for the commemorative meeting. The students hosting the commemorative meeting kept stepping forward to ask them to leave the podium. Each time they asked, the detectives always maintained that indifferent attitude. At 9:00 AM, the school authorities' representatives, Dean of the Law School Zhou Binglin and Dean of Studies Fan Jichang, arrived at the same time. At this time, a dozen police officers entered the auditorium and tore down the slogans pasted on the walls, indiscriminately, leaving only a cloth banner and a pair of cloth couplets. The banner boldly read "May Fourth 17th Anniversary Commemoration Meeting," and the couplets read: "Lost territory and sovereignty, today's worthies are inferior to those of the past, how can we bear to listen to the orders of the bandit police, sitting idly by and letting them be completely destroyed?" "Save the nation and resist the enemy, dying is more glorious than living, vowing to dedicate ourselves to the nation, striving for liberation and success."

At 9:00 AM sharp, the meeting was announced to begin. More than a dozen plainclothes detectives mingled among the three or four hundred students and attended the meeting together. Someone proposed organizing a temporary security team and asking the plainclothes detectives to leave the venue, but Zhou Binglin immediately dismissed the idea with a few words. He said, "This is absolutely impossible. We are already fortunate to be allowed to hold the meeting. In this situation, what freedom do we have? Moreover, plainclothes detectives are always following us anytime, anywhere. Since we are holding an open and honest meeting today, what do we have to fear from them?"

Students and Professors Roar Like Lions

The program of the commemorative meeting was very simple, with only two items, professors' speeches and students' speeches, being considered the most important. This program, it is said, was also approved by the school authorities. A total of three students spoke. Some of them said, "I hope that the external expressions will not be as enthusiastic and high-pitched as the internal feelings." Others said, "No matter what, we must strive diligently within the constraints of the environment." While speaking, they clenched their fists and frowned, and their inner anguish was obvious at a glance.

Later, the chairman repeatedly invited students to come on stage and express their opinions, but everyone looked at each other and hesitated to come forward. The Peking University students, who were always eager to express their opinions, seemed to be a little cautious in such an environment.

Not many professors arrived. The few who participated probably came after receiving the news at the last minute. A total of five people expressed their opinions: Ma Xulun, Zhou Binglin, Fan Jichang, Xu Deheng, and Zeng Zhaolun.

Ma Xulun, who is over fifty years old and has graying hair, has held important positions such as Deputy Minister of Education and Director of Civil Affairs of Zhejiang Province. He is an old professor at Peking University. During the "May Fourth" Movement seventeen years ago, Ma personally participated in the event at the school. Therefore, what he said was quite cordial and meaningful. His main points were twofold: striving is valuable only in the darkness, so seventeen years ago, he strongly opposed the southward relocation of the school; those who strive for the liberation of the masses will eventually achieve victory. His gestures during the speech were both solemn and humorous, captivating the audience. At such an advanced age, he teaches courses in Lao-Zhuang philosophy at Peking University while tirelessly running around and appealing for national affairs. In January of this year, he was the first to sign the first declaration of the National Salvation Association of the cultural circles in this city, and, along with Ma Xiangbo, the 96-year-old who first signed the declaration of the National Salvation Association of the cultural circles in Shanghai, was admired by the people of the country.

Dean of the Law School Zhou Binglin, who has held important positions such as Director of the Hebei Department of Education, has a deep relationship with the party-state and is resented by officials of a certain country. Last year, he was subjected to several expulsions and threats, but he remained unmoved. Since the student movement occurred, he has consistently expressed his views from the government's standpoint. However, because his words are quite measured, the resentment he has incurred is not very deep. In his speech, after recounting various memories of studying at Peking University and participating in the "May Fourth" Movement seventeen years ago, he still maintained his inherent position, advising students to study hard and prepare themselves for future service to the country. His speech was organized and concise, just like the man himself.

Dean of Studies Fan Jichang, standing in the position of the school authorities, advised students to maintain their passionate spirit and seek outlets in worthwhile areas.

Zeng Zhaolun's speech was organized and orderly, befitting the true colors of a chemist. He advised students to be unsung heroes and not just well-known heroes.

Xu Deheng's speech clarified the origin of the "May Fourth" Movement from the perspective of emerging sociology and affirmed that the significance of the "May Fourth" Movement was threefold: the masses directly entered the political movement; it was an organized movement; it was a widespread social movement. He also said that the current international and domestic situation has undergone great changes, and the "May Fourth" Movement is no longer sufficient. So, how will we use the spirit of the "May Fourth" to advance the social movement? While speaking, he raised his arms and shouted, and his spittle flew everywhere.

The meeting adjourned at 11:30 AM. Under the supervision of the military police, everyone filed out in an orderly manner. The 17th anniversary commemoration of the "May Fourth" Movement thus came to an end.

Local News

Statistics on Tax Revenue Losses from Smuggling in North China - Reaching Over 25 Million in Nine Months - Approximately One-Third of Total Tax Revenue 74

Report from Customs Authorities

According to the Central News Agency, smuggling incidents in North China have intensified since February of this year, impacting customs revenue. The extent of this impact is of great interest to all parties. This is because a large number of our domestic and foreign debts are guaranteed by customs revenue. Therefore, smuggling incidents under the protection of the Japanese are by no means ordinary local issues. Their impact, politically, not only involves China and Japan but also has a significant relationship with the great powers. Furthermore, the customs' anti-smuggling system has improved rapidly since 1933 and can compete with the anti-smuggling systems of other countries. Therefore, if there are no special circumstances, the eradication of smuggling is almost an easy matter. The crux of the problem is therefore clear. The Central News Agency now reports the important points and figures regarding this matter from the customs authorities, as follows:

From August 1st of last year to April 30th of this year, customs revenue losses due to smuggling in North China totaled 25,506,146 yuan.

In April of this year alone, customs revenue losses reached 8 million yuan.

From August of last year to March of this year, the average monthly loss was 1.7 million yuan.

Since April 1st of this year, the rampant increase in smuggled goods has been unprecedented.

Assuming a monthly loss of 8 million yuan, the annual loss will reach 96 million yuan, accounting for almost one-third of the total tax revenue.

During the week of April 19th to 25th of this year, smuggled goods transported from Qinhuangdao, Beidaihe, Nandaisi, Liushouying, and Changli to Tianjin were as follows:

From August 1st of last year to April 25th of this year, the total amount of smuggled goods transported to Tianjin was as follows:

The miscellaneous goods mentioned above include dried seafood, kerosene, food, ammonia water, rubber, tires, rubber shoes, tinplate, paints, and sulfuric acid, etc.

During the week of April 19th to 25th of this year, smuggled goods transported from Tianjin via the Beining Railway and Pinghan Railway to other parts of China were approximately as follows:

In a report released yesterday, the customs authorities stated that the smuggling situation in North China last year can be roughly divided into three periods: the first period, from January to the end of May of last year, during which Japanese and "Manchukuo" people frequently smuggled silver coins. Two smuggling incidents on May 17th and May 25th were detected by the authorities, and the Japanese side immediately made demands, causing the customs to be in a rather difficult position. During this period, maritime smuggling had not yet expanded, and large-scale smuggling had not yet matured. However, from April to May, there was a large amount of silver coin smuggling, amounting to about 177,000 yuan. The second period, from June to mid-September of last year, during which the Japanese side made demands that were accepted by our side. By September, customs anti-smuggling vessels were forced to be unable to perform their duties in the war zone, and at the same time, anti-smuggling personnel along the Great Wall were disarmed. At this time, the smuggling problem gradually became serious. Customs personnel were no longer allowed to carry pistols, and as a result, lawbreakers became more active. According to estimates, there were about 400 Korean ruffians engaged in smuggling in Shanhaiguan and 100 in Qinhuangdao. By mid-September, Shihe Transport Company, which specializes in smuggling, appeared, employing as many as 1,000 Chinese coolies. Thus, open smuggling began. These lawbreakers all carried wooden sticks and pistols. If customs personnel showed the slightest intention of interfering, they would be beaten by these people, resulting in serious injuries, with no one to complain to. However, during this period, in addition to smuggling silver coins for export, the only smuggled goods imported were rayon, which was transported via the Beining Railway to other parts of the country. The railway authorities, under duress, had no choice but to allow its transport and were unable to resist. The Chinese side repeatedly requested assistance from the Japanese military authorities, but the Japanese side claimed that the matter should be handled by the Japanese police, and when a request was made to the Japanese police, they claimed that smuggling into China did not violate Japanese law, so the Japanese police were powerless. By September, the situation had expanded further. On the 9th of that month, the Japanese military authorities demanded that the Qinhuangdao Customs Commissioner remove all machine guns placed on customs anti-smuggling vessels. Although the customs authorities argued on the basis of reason, the Japanese side turned a deaf ear. As a result, the customs had no choice but to yield. A few days later, the Japanese side made another demand that all anti-smuggling vessels, whether armed or unarmed, be prohibited from sailing within three English miles of the war zone. The Chinese side, yielding to pressure, had reason but could not assert it. As a result, customs anti-smuggling vessels disappeared from the war zone. The matter was reported to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which made several serious protests to the Japanese Ambassador to China, with no results. The third period, from mid-September to the end of December of last year, during which the customs' anti-smuggling management can be said to have completely disappeared. The Japanese naval authorities completely denied China's three-mile territorial sea rights and regarded the search of customs anti-smuggling vessels as piracy, resulting in the complete disappearance of anti-smuggling effectiveness. As a result, maritime transport could not be controlled, and private ships from Dalian along the coast were constantly arriving. The authorities could only sigh helplessly. Since January of this year, in addition to maritime transport, there has also been land transport. Although the customs has repeatedly requested assistance from the railway authorities and the Japanese police, there have been no results. Recently, after the pseudo-organization of eastern Hebei set its own tax rates, the problem has become even more complicated. The Japanese authorities are making things difficult everywhere, saying that once goods have been taxed in eastern Hebei, they cannot be taxed again elsewhere, which shows that the tax rates set by eastern Hebei have been approved by the Japanese side. The customs report also stated that the seriousness of the smuggling problem in North China is even more alarming from another perspective. North China has always been a base for the transportation of goods. All goods transported south from Tianjin-Pukou and Pinghan Railways can directly reach the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. The bulk of China's total tax revenue is in the northern part of the Yangtze River. Now, smuggled goods from North China are continuously transported south, and their impact on the national treasury income not only involves a corner of the north. According to last year's statistics, 88.8% of the total tax revenue was collected by 21 seaports from Qinhuangdao to Ningbo. It can be seen that private smuggling in North China directly affects 88% of the national income. The importance of the incident is evident. (To be continued tomorrow)

China National Products Maintenance Association - Cables Request for Strict Anti-Smuggling - Punishing According to Law to Maintain Chinese Rights and Save National Products - Newly Appointed Executive Supervisors Held Swearing-In Ceremony Last Night 75

The China National Products Maintenance Association held a swearing-in ceremony for the new executive supervisors last night and held the first joint meeting of the executive supervisors. Regarding the smuggling problem in North China, it was decided to cable the government to strictly crack down on smuggling in order to maintain the national product market. The details are as follows:

Swearing-In Ceremony

The China National Products Maintenance Association held the 24th new executive supervisor committee swearing-in ceremony at the Dahongyun Restaurant at 6:00 PM last night. The smuggling problem in North China is becoming increasingly serious, affecting the national financial lifeline. There are still many important cases that cannot be discussed further due to the late hour, and they will be discussed at the next meeting. The meeting adjourned at around 9:00 PM.

Cabling for Anti-Smuggling

The original cable read: To President Jiang of the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, and Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry: Recently, in North China, foreign nationals have been relying on special forces to smuggle large quantities of goods into China for dumping, and recently, it has spread throughout the country. The market is becoming increasingly rampant. Not only are Chinese goods and industries suffering the most, but they are also on the verge of death, and the shortage of our national tax revenue is enough to affect the national financial lifeline. If this continues, the consequences will be unimaginable. Such acts that endanger sovereignty and violate public law have long been noticed by countries around the world. The association, in order to maintain national products, is forced to make a special appeal. We earnestly request that Your Excellency the President quickly devise effective methods to urge the relevant agencies to strictly investigate and crack down on smuggling, punish them according to law, and thereby maintain sovereignty and save national products. We await your orders with bated breath. Wang Jiean, Wang Xingyi, and Huang Chucai, standing committee members of the China National Products Maintenance Association, respectfully kowtow.

Polish Officials and侨民 Commemorate Piłsudski - Yesterday Was the Anniversary of His Death - The Polish Legation Lowered Its Flag to Half-Mast to Mourn 80

May 12th was the anniversary of the death of General Piłsudski, a founding father of the Polish nation. The Polish Legation in this port specially lowered its flag to half-mast yesterday to mourn and took a day off. All Polish侨民 living in Shanghai also closed their businesses and stopped entertainment. At 8:00 AM yesterday, Polish侨民 held a memorial prayer service at the church on Sainte Marie Road. It was decided that a large-scale memorial meeting would be held at the YMCA on Jing'an Temple Road at 3:00 PM on the 17th. All Polish officials and侨民 will participate, and Polish Minister Weidengtao will attend and deliver a speech. It is reported that Piłsudski died of illness at 8:45 PM on May 12th last year at the Belvedere Palace in Warsaw, Poland, at the age of 68. Piłsudski was born on December 5, 1867, and studied medicine at a Russian university. At that time, Poland was suffering from the pain of being partitioned. Piłsudski devoted himself to revolutionary work and was arrested repeatedly, but his revolutionary work did not stop. He was once exiled to Siberia. During the five years of the European war, Piłsudski secretly organized volunteer armies in various parts of Poland to resist Russia and fight for Polish independence, winning successive victories. In 1917, Piłsudski was imprisoned by the German government in a military prison. The following year, the Great War ended, and Piłsudski was finally freed, and Poland finally achieved independence with Piłsudski's efforts. A provisional government was established, and he was elected as its leader. When the formal constitution was completed, although he was elected as the first president, he firmly declined and retired to the post of Minister of Military Affairs. In 1920, he defeated the Russian army that invaded Poland again, and his reputation grew even greater. He was regarded as a national hero by the world. When he died last year, commentators generally said that Poland had lost its only leader from then on, which was indeed the most significant loss.

Letter from the Money Trade Association Requesting All Firms to Comply with Orders and Rectify Business Practices, and Thoroughly Investigate the Debts of Firms That Have Voluntarily Closed 81

The New Sound News Agency reports that, in order to rescue the money trade, the Ministry of Finance established a Money Trade Supervision Committee at the end of April last year. At the same time, it ordered the rectification of business practices. Now the Money Trade Association has received another letter from the Supervision Committee, transcribing the instructions from the Ministry of Finance, ordering compliance with last year's directives and informing all firms to rectify any non-compliant points in their business operations. The Association has already complied with these instructions.

Investigating Firms That Have Voluntarily Closed

The following money shops voluntarily closed before and after the closing of accounts in the 24th year of the Republic of China: Yi Sheng Shop, No. [address] Jiyang Lane, Henan Road, North City; Zhi Cheng Shop, No. [address] Jiyang Lane, Henan Road, North City; Ze Chang Shop, No. [address] Jixiang Lane, Henan Road, North City; Fu Tai Shop, No. [address] Qingshun Lane, Beijing Road, North City. Various money shops previously borrowed 25 million yuan from the Bank of China, Central Bank, and Communications Bank. Apart from the 7 million yuan from various commercial banks and the Money Trade Joint Reserve, which has been fully repaid, only slightly more than 12 million yuan of the 18 million yuan from the Bank of China, Central Bank, and Communications Bank remains outstanding from Heng [莊名] and a few other money shops. Efforts are currently being made to repay it. It has been verified that the above loans are secured by reliable collateral, such as land deeds, goods, and bonds. The interest rate is 8% per annum. In order to thoroughly regulate the money trade finance, the Bank of China, Central Bank, and Communications Bank have made special accommodations, allowing repeated extensions for repayment.

Regulations on the Carrying of Silver Small Coins and Copper Coins by Passengers and Crew; Jianghai Customs Proclamation Limiting Amounts 84

The Jianghai Customs, in order to comply with orders regulating the carrying of silver small coins by passengers and crew, has issued Proclamation No. 15-2, which states: "Concerning the method of applying for passports for transporting silver and the penalties for secretly carrying it, proclamations have been issued several times. Now, in compliance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, the item of silver small coins, which are still temporarily allowed to be used as circulating subsidiary currency, has not been included within the scope of silver. Special regulations are hereby made regarding the carrying method as follows: 1. Passengers traveling to and from the interior may carry silver small coins in accordance with the regulations of this Customs Proclamation No. 1393 of October 30, 23rd year of the Republic of China, regardless of single or double coins, up to 300 coins per person. 2. Passengers traveling along the coast should, at this time when new subsidiary currency is being issued, take the carrying of new subsidiary currency as the principle. If new subsidiary currency is not yet widely circulating, and the Central Bank, Bank of China, Communications Bank, and Farmers Bank of China subsidiary currency notes are also not circulating locally, the carrying of silver small coins will be temporarily permitted, but regardless of single or double coins, not more than 60 coins per person. 3. Crew members and sailors navigating domestically may carry silver small coins, regardless of single or double coins, not more than 60 coins per person. 4. For all passengers, crew members, and sailors entering or leaving Zhejiang Province, the carrying of silver small coins, regardless of single or double coins, is limited to 50 coins per person. As for passengers traveling to and from the interior of the province under its jurisdiction, the number of silver small coins they may carry is still handled according to the general rule of 300 coins per person. 5. There is no need to apply for a passport to report the transport of silver small coins for export, but silver export tax and equalization tax should be levied in accordance with the regulations of this Customs Proclamation No. 1389 of October 15, 23rd year of the Republic of China. 6. For sailing boats operating along Qingdao, Longkou, Yantai, and the coastal area, the total number of silver coins that passengers and boatmen may carry per boat should not exceed 100 yuan, as stipulated in this Customs Proclamation No. 1455 issued on July 15th of last year. Since the implementation of legal tender, this ordinance has been generally abolished. As for the carrying of silver small coins, the carrying of new subsidiary currency should also be taken as the principle. If new subsidiary currency is not yet widely circulating, and the Central Bank, Bank of China, Communications Bank, and Farmers Bank of China subsidiary currency notes are also not circulating locally, each sailing boat passenger and boatman may temporarily carry silver small coins, regardless of single or double coins, up to a total of 120 coins. 7. Furthermore, passengers entering or leaving Zhejiang Province may carry up to 1,000 single copper coins per person. However, passengers traveling to other places in the country and those traveling to and from within the jurisdiction of Zhejiang Province may still carry up to 5,000 single copper coins per person in accordance with this Customs Proclamation No. 1393 issued on October 30, 23rd year of the Republic of China. Let all merchants and people be universally aware of this. This proclamation is hereby issued."

After the Hesheng Steamer Ran Aground in Tianjin, the Xinming Was Damaged by a Collision 85

The China Merchants Bureau's regular North China steamer Xinming, with a displacement of 2,143 tons, a length of 270 feet, a breadth of 41 feet and 2 inches, a depth of 20 feet and 2 inches, and a draft of 15 feet, was loaded with passengers and goods in Tianjin and first went to Weihaiwei and Yantai before returning to Shanghai. As the Xinming steamer was sailing out of the Baihe River, the British Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Hesheng steamer, with a displacement of 2,194 tons, was fully loaded with cargo and was sailing from South China and Shanghai to North China. When the steamer arrived at Xuegu and was sailing into the Baihe River, the Xinming had not yet left Zizhulin. Unexpectedly, because the Hesheng was overloaded with cargo and had too deep a draft, it suddenly ran aground and the hull was stranded in the sea and could not be moved. Because its grounding obstructed the channel, the Xinming wanted to sail to a shallower area, resulting in a collision. The Xinming was struck by Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Hesheng steamer. Because the Hesheng steamer from Dagu to Tianjin exceeded the waterline limit set by the customs, the pilot received a report stating that Jardine Matheson's Hesheng had already notified Dagu, saying that it had run aground in the Haihe River. The vessel (i.e., the Xinming) sailed out of Tianjin and collided with that steamer. The extent of the damage has been reported to the Tianjin authorities. The responsibility for the damage to this vessel lies entirely with the British steamer. When this vessel arrives in Shanghai, it will be necessary to notify the company to send a surveyor to the vessel to inspect the damage. Please consider this matter. Upon receiving the report, the China Merchants Bureau notified the insurance company and prepared to inspect the damage when the Xinming arrived in Shanghai in order to prepare for negotiations. As for the Hesheng steamer, it is hoped that it can be unloaded and towed out during high tide.

The Rice Industry Has Not Ordered Foreign Rice 86

Although there are still stockpiles, the amount is very small. Orders were also given to instruct rice merchants to purchase and stockpile domestic rice as much as possible.

Regarding the matter of the Ministry of Finance's approval of the request to prevent the dumping of foreign rice, the reporter from the Central News Agency inquired with various relevant parties. According to a spokesperson for the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, after receiving instructions from the Municipal Government regarding the matter of the Ministry of Finance's request to prevent the dumping of foreign rice, the bureau conducted an investigation into the rice industry in this city. The investigation found that the rice industry in this city is not currently ordering foreign rice. Although there are still stockpiles of foreign rice in Shanghai, the amount is very small. The foreign broken rice previously ordered from foreign merchants has mostly been resold to foreign rice merchants en route due to price factors. In addition to ordering rice merchants to purchase domestic rice as much as possible in the future, the bureau also submitted the findings of the investigation to the Municipal Government for submission to the Ministry of Finance for its reference. According to inquiries from rice merchants, the Yongshang Chamber of Commerce ordered foreign broken rice from foreign merchants for disaster relief purposes, so it was approved by the Ministry of Finance to be exempt from all taxes, which has nothing to do with Shanghai merchants. Therefore, the various statements made by the Wujiang County Chamber of Commerce are clearly misrepresentations. Now that the price of domestic rice is low, it is impossible to purchase foreign rice. Therefore, most of the previously ordered foreign broken rice has not been shipped to the country for sale, but has been resold to foreign merchants abroad.

In addition to reporting to the Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea Transportation and Sales Committee, this announcement is hereby made. Address: No. 190 Beijing Road, Shanghai. Telephone: 12613, 12923."

Discussion of Solutions Yesterday

It is reported that the black tea issue is being negotiated by the Foreign Tea Industry Association with the Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea Transportation and Sales Committee. Liu Yuanze of the Foreign Tea Industry Association is very much in favor of the establishment of a tea company. Specific methods still need to be discussed. Shanghai Postal Administration Notification No. 1329 states that, starting from the 17th of this month, the parcel mailing and receiving offices of this bureau will be open from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM on Sundays and public holidays for mailing and delivering various domestic parcels. This notification is hereby issued for general knowledge. The items are as follows: 1. Hypodermic syringes and needles; 2. Narcotics; 3. Films; 4. Radio equipment; 5. Cigarettes and tobacco; 6. Cigarette paper; 7. Revenue stamps and tax bills; 8. Silver bars or loose silver; 9. Gold; 10. Military supplies; 11. Sodium cyanide. Bureau Director Zha Peilin, May 12.

Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant Directly Transmitting Electricity to Taicang, Jiading, and Baoshan Counties 103

Baoshan County Has Now Been Fully Installed, Taicang and Jiading Counties Are Actively Erecting Poles and Lines

The Huashang Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, considering that the electricity for lighting in the neighboring counties of Taicang, Jiading, and Baoshan is insufficient, resulting in very weak lighting, and in order to support rural construction, has planned to be responsible for transmitting electricity from the plant. Baoshan County has now been fully installed and will implement county-wide transmission starting on June 1st. Taicang and Jiading counties are still in the planning stage and can also be implemented soon. The details are as follows:

Baoshan County to Implement on June 1st

The electricity for lighting in Dachang, Guzhai, Liuhang, Yuepu, and Baoshan County City in Zhabei Baoshan County has been provided by the Dachang Da Yao Electric Lighting Plant. Recently, due to the vast area, the original generators are insufficient, resulting in very weak lighting. Manager Wang Yingru of the plant signed a contract with the Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant, and the Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant will directly transmit electricity. Dachang, Guzhai, Liuhang, and other places in Baoshan have already been implemented. In addition, Luodian Town previously had the Yao Ming Electric Lighting Plant, but the machinery was old and damaged, causing the current to be interrupted from time to time. After consultation between the local Chamber of Commerce and Wang Yingru, it was decided that the Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant would directly supply power. All installations have now been completed and will be implemented on June 1st. The surrounding towns and villages near Luodian will also be supplied by the Luodian distribution square shed. Therefore, the electricity for the entire Baoshan County will be directly supplied by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant starting on June 1st, and lighting will be available every night, which will also help promote rural construction.

Jiading and Taicang Counties Are Under Planning

Jiading and Taicang counties also have their own electric lighting plants. In order to support the local industries, it was decided to follow the same method as Baoshan County, consult with the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, and request the same electricity transmission. Both parties have agreed and signed a contract to install poles and lines along the Xihu Highway for direct transmission, and to build a square in Jiading and Taicang counties to transfer power to various towns and cities in the two counties. The initial construction will begin next month, but the electric poles in the two counties are still in good condition, making the project easier. It is expected to be completed in August.

Page 12

Failure to Distribute Russian Oil, Clearing Debts: Guanghua Company Transfers to Asiatic, Will Fully Repay Loans from Four Banks Including Shanghai Bank, Machines, Oil Tanks, etc. Sold for Over Four Million Yuan - Company Name Still in Use, Only Distributing British and American Oil - 106

The Huashang Guanghua Petroleum Co., Ltd. at 14 Museum Road, Shanghai, due to manager Russian oil merchant You Biandi competing with British and American oil merchants, has incurred huge debts. In order to protect its debts and clear its credit, the company has painfully sacrificed and transferred to the British Asiatic Petroleum Co. However, the company's future business will be supplied and distributed by British and American oil merchants. The reporter of Dagong News Agency has obtained reliable information, which is recorded as follows:

Guanghua History The Huashang Guanghua Petroleum Co., Ltd. was initiated in the Republic of China Year 17 by Mr. Xu Shiying, the current Chinese Ambassador to Japan, and others. At the beginning, the capital was only 500,000. The company managed American Mobil Oil and sold it in various places. The business gradually developed. In the Republic of China Year 18, the capital was increased to more than 1.1 million. From Year 19 to Year 20, it increased from 1.5 million to 3.6 million. The internal business was divided into kerosene and gasoline departments. The oil depots were located at Laoshusha along the Huangpu River in Pudong and Danshuichi in Hankou. The chairman of the company is Xu Shiying, and the managing director and general manager is Jing Yidou. The company is the only Chinese-owned oil enterprise in China, and the good impression it gives to the Chinese people must be attributed to Xu Shiying's hard work and the efforts of all directors and supervisors.

Distribution of Russian Oil When the company was first established in the Republic of China Year 17, it originally planned to undertake large-scale operations, hoping to develop the large amount of oil reserves in various provinces in China, such as Sichuan and Xinjiang. However, due to limited capital, it was unable to shoulder this heavy responsibility. Therefore, it temporarily managed American Mobil Oil. After careful planning and determined management, it had a surplus of more than 2.5 million in the past three or four years. In the spring of the Republic of China Year 20, UP.T (transliterated as You Biandi), a Russian oil merchant, wanted to develop a market in the Far East and compete with British and American oil merchants. However, there was no market base (i.e., distribution points and oil storage tanks). Therefore, they repeatedly consulted with Guanghua Company to discuss how to withdraw Mobil Oil and switch to distributing Russian oil. After a long period of consultation, a contract was finally signed. Guanghua Company immediately withdrew from managing American oil and officially accepted the distribution of Russian oil.

Competition Among Three Countries After the Russian merchants solved the problem of the oil sales market in China, they used their large amount of oil production to dump oil in China. Before the Russian oil market in the Republic of China Year 20, the oil prices of British Asiatic and American Mobil Texaco were the highest, and the selling price was more than ten yuan per box. When Russian oil was first shipped to China, it was about nine yuan per box. The oil merchants of that country wanted to control the expansion of the British and American oil market, so they depreciated and dumped oil. The lowest price was only six yuan and six jiao per box. Sales soared, and British and American oil merchants also reduced prices to compete, and the market suddenly became chaotic. This was truly an unprecedented initiative in the history of the oil industry.

Borrowing for Construction When British, American, and Russian oil merchants were fiercely competing, Guanghua Company, although in a distribution position, did not bear any operating losses. However, in order to store a large amount of oil reserves, and to transport ships and machinery, it was necessary to have sufficient preparation. Therefore, the company specially borrowed five million yuan from four banks in Shanghai, the Mainland, Guohuo, and Guohua, using the land and oil tanks as collateral. After the loan was established, in addition to expanding the original oil depot in Laoshusha, Pudong, it also added oil tanks in Danshuichi, Hankou, costing more than 4.5 million yuan. The full term of the loan contract was limited to July of the Republic of China Year 24. Later, Russian oil suffered too much loss due to competition, and the pain was deep. Therefore, the contract with Guanghua was terminated. Now Russian oil has completely abandoned the Far East market.

State-Owned Operation Failed The company's total capital was eventually increased to 3.6 million yuan. Later, it purchased machinery and built oil tanks, and borrowed another five million yuan from the bank, plus the surplus of more than 2 million yuan when managing American oil, totaling more than 10 million yuan. During the competition among the three oil merchants, it lost two or three million yuan over three years. But in fact, the company itself did not lose money, and what it owed was now converted into various construction fixed assets. At a difficult time, it applied to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry for a loan of 10 million yuan for relief, to be taken over by the government as a state-owned enterprise. When Minister Chen Gongbo was in charge of the Ministry of Industry, he sent the Mining Department to Shanghai to investigate, and all agreed that this enterprise should be supported by the state to avoid falling into the hands of foreigners. Unfortunately, due to the depletion of the national treasury, they were sincere but powerless, and it failed to become a reality.

Transfer to British Merchants In order to maintain the repayment of bank debts and credit, the company painfully sacrificed and now sold the base of the oil land in Laoshusha, Pudong, to the Shanghai Commercial and Savings Bank for 960,000 yuan, to repay the bank's debt. It also transferred various equipment such as machines, oil tanks, and ships to the British Asiatic Petroleum Co. for more than 3.2 million yuan. Both parties have signed the agreement. At the same time, the American Mobil Oil Co. has also joined as a transferee and cooperated with the British Asiatic. The Guanghua Company authorities have now fully repaid the overdue debts of the bank.

Business As Usual According to the Dagong News Agency's investigation from both the British Asiatic and Guanghua Company, although Guanghua Company has fully transferred the oil tanks and other properties to the British merchants, the company's future business will be supplied by the British Asiatic and Mobil oil merchants. However, its total business volume shall not exceed one-tenth of the total annual volume of the British and American companies, that is, the kerosene distribution quantity shall not exceed 100,000 boxes. The distribution commission part is still under negotiation. As for the Guanghua name, it will still be used externally, and the oil sales area can be operated in the market base of British and American merchants in China. (Dagong News Agency)

Municipal Federation of Trade Unions Petitions the Central Government for Prior Payment of Labor Creditors 114

According to Dagong News Agency, in recent years, the city's economy has been depressed, and all industries have been declining. Factories and shops have closed down and declared liquidation every day. However, regarding the issue of labor creditors' rights obtained from sweat and blood, which should be given the highest priority in repayment, although various parties have requested it, there are no clear provisions in the current laws. In order to protect the due rights of workers, the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions has followed the resolution of the Fourth All-City Workers' Congress and specially prepared a document to be submitted to the Central Political Committee, the Executive Yuan, and the Legislative Yuan, requesting that laws be formulated and promulgated for implementation. The original petition is recorded as follows: A petition requesting the stipulation that labor creditors' rights should have the right to be repaid first in order to maintain the livelihood of workers. I have secretly investigated the current laws and regulations, and there are no provisions for the priority of repayment of rights obtained by workers due to employment relations. For example, Article 35 of the Trade Union Law stipulates that "when the debtor of food and wages goes bankrupt, he has the right to request priority repayment of his property." As for the factory and the section on employment in the Civil Code, there are only principles for the payment methods, locations, and periods of wages. There is no mention of the priority of wage repayment. There is no word mentioned. The recently promulgated bankruptcy law has a total of 112 articles, although there is a clear statement that "debts with priority rights over the property of the bankrupt property group shall be repaid before other debts," but it does not enumerate what kind of debts are stipulated. Therefore, when an employer goes bankrupt or closes down, workers' wages and other debts arising from employment relations (such as security deposits, public accumulation funds, etc.) cannot be clearly claimed and repaid first according to the law, and the court cannot base its judgment on its right to be repaid first. Often, the lawsuit ends in victory, but the result cannot be enforced. This is because in recent years, the city's economy has been sluggish, and most employers are strong on the outside but weak on the inside. All their assets are mortgaged to banks and money shops for maintenance, and these creditors' rights obtained due to mortgage rights or pledge rights all have priority in law. If an employer goes bankrupt or closes down, his property will be seized by the pledgees and pledgees. Workers will eventually be unable to seek compensation. Even if the government mediates and arbitrates and is lucky enough to get some share, the exchange of letters and telegrams is already a greater loss than gain. This is a common phenomenon in recent years and is the biggest crisis in society. If a way to stabilize is not sought quickly, it will inevitably affect the entire social security and make the country and the nation suffer endless influence. The workers' creditors' rights are purely obtained from sweat and hard work and are the basis of the whole family's life. The nature of these creditors' rights is completely different from other creditors' rights. If they are not given the right to be repaid first, their livelihood will be cut off. Is this not the fairness of things? Modern laws tend to be socialized, with the principle of protecting the economically weak and maintaining the welfare of the majority. Therefore, all advanced industrial countries stipulate that workers' creditors' rights obtained due to employment relations have the right to be repaid first. This is because workers have a low economic status. Without close protection, it is not enough to prevent illegal infringements. In view of the domestic industrial and commercial difficulties and the difficult livelihood of workers, the association has, through the Fourth Congress of Representatives, resolved to petition the central government to stipulate that labor creditors' rights should have the right to prior repayment. It is specially written to petition Jun (Hui) (Yuan), requesting that the Legislative Yuan be consulted and urgently formulate laws and promulgate them for implementation in order to maintain the livelihood of workers and maintain social order. Respectfully presented to the Central Executive Committee, the Executive Yuan, and the Legislative Yuan.

The Sino-Foreign Relief Committee Dispatches a Special Commissioner to Inspect the Anhui Disaster, Continued Report 115

The Sino-Foreign Relief Committee on Renji Road, considering the severity of the drought in northern Anhui, has already distributed 4,800 yuan to Huo Qiu, 4,800 yuan to Fuyang, 3,000 yuan to Shou County, 2,400 yuan to Yingshang, 1,500 yuan to Taihe, 1,500 yuan to Linchuan (transliteration), 1,000 yuan to Fengtai, and 1,000 yuan to Guoyang. In addition to setting up a branch in Fuyang to actively carry out relief efforts, they have also dispatched a special commissioner to inspect the situation and ascertain the truth. According to the report, the investigation into the situation in Shou County was previously published. Now, the report continues with an on-site survey of the disaster conditions in Zhengyangguan and Yingshang County, recorded as follows: Zhengyangguan, although belonging to the fifth district of Shou County, actually occupies four-tenths of the county's area, and the disaster area accounts for seven-tenths of that. The losses amount to more than 1.4 million yuan, lasting for five months. Over 70,000 people are awaiting relief, so special attention must be paid. Walking more than ten li from the South Gate to the East Gate, one sees disaster victims mostly eating wild vegetables. If this continues for a few more days, the situation is unimaginable. Moreover, the land and water transportation there is relatively convenient, so many people fleeing famine from neighboring counties have also come there, making the situation even more precarious. Continuing to Huo Qiu, the Fuyang branch of the committee had just allocated 4,800 yuan for relief, divided into three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan levels for distribution. Those in special circumstances receive an additional five jiao. Details of the distribution will be reported later. Proceeding to Yingshang, the county is located between the Huai and Ying Rivers, bordering Huo Qiu to the south. The area has always been known for its poverty and suffering. Since the major flood of Xinwei year, there have been consecutive years of famine. This year's spring famine is particularly severe. Disaster victims mostly dig up grass roots and tree bark to prolong their lives, and many have starved to death. There are also cases of selling wives and children to exchange for grain to fill their hunger, and even entire families committing suicide, the situation is extremely tragic. The county is divided into three districts, but the second district has the widest disaster area, especially in places like Nanzhao and Gengpeng Runhe. The third district, north of the Ying River, is also severely affected. The first district is slightly better. With the arrival of the spring famine, the county government has actively established more than twenty porridge kitchens, with more than three thousand people coming to the city to eat every day. However, funds are tight, and without substantial financial assistance, disaster victims will inevitably starve to death, it is said.

The Fish Market Opens Yesterday, Salted Fish Merchants Are Allowed to Operate as Usual 122

According to the Industry Department, the Shanghai Fish Market of the Industry Department opened at 3:00 AM yesterday. It is estimated that two iced fresh fishing boats and fifteen sailing boats were involved in the transaction, and the value of fish sold was more than 10,000 gold. The remaining goods are stored in the market's cold storage. According to Article 2 of the Fish Market Regulations, salted dried fish is also within the scope of transactions. The 57 members of the Shanghai Salted Fish Industry Association believed that salted dried fish had special circumstances and could not be sold at the fish market. After an emergency meeting of the association, it was decided to send representatives Jin Chuxiang, Lou Wenzhi, Chen Zuyu, Liu Zhiyuan, and others to the Fish Market Council with a letter at 4:00 PM yesterday to state the business situation. The Fish Market Council Chairman Du Yuesheng, Standing Director Yu Qiaqing, and Kui Yanfang met with them. The representatives stated four ways of operating by the members: 1. Ordering imported salted dried fish from foreign merchants; 2. Self-purchasing salted dried fish from outside the pass; 3. Self-manufacturing salted dried fish in the fishing area; 4. Lending money to fishermen and merchants to transport and sell salted dried fish; and requested to be allowed to operate as usual. Du and others replied that salted dried fish does have special circumstances, and it has been decided by the board of directors that they will not be auctioned at the fish market, and salted fish merchants can still operate as usual. It is also planned to discuss solutions with the persons in charge of the Salted Fish Industry Association at a later date. The representatives believed that the result was satisfactory, and then took their leave and returned.

The preparatory meeting for the 15th Health Movement in this city was held at 2:00 PM yesterday at the YMCA on Sichuan Road. Shen Gao chaired the meeting, and Wu Zhongyao recorded the minutes. The meeting is recorded as follows:

After the formalities, Chairman Shen Gao first made a report, stating briefly that various sectors of this city hold a health movement every year, and this has now reached the 15th session, but each session has its own special points of attention. The focus of this session is on child health and maternal and infant health. The Health Bureau has already drafted the plan for this session's health movement and the charter of the association. I hope that all representatives will express their opinions to make this session's health movement have a successful outcome. In addition, this city has decided that this health movement will be held in conjunction with the Summer Health Movement organized by the New Life Movement General Association in various places, according to the instructions of Instructor Wu, and the New Life Movement Promotion Association of this city.

Representative Report

Following this, Zhu Jiarang of the New Life Movement Promotion Association reported, stating briefly that this city's annual routine health movement coincided with the fact that the New Life Movement in this city had also recently received a notice from the Movement General Association, issuing a detailed outline of the Summer Health Movement plan, ordering the holding of the Summer Health Movement. Instructor Wu and Permanent Secretary Pan and others all advocated that it be held in conjunction with this session's health movement. Therefore, the outline of the plan has been sent to this meeting, hoping to use it as a reference for cooperation.

Discussion of Proposals

After the report, the discussion began. - The association's charter was discussed and resolved to be amended and passed. - The association's work plan outline was discussed and resolved to be amended and passed. - The association's budget was discussed and resolved to be amended and passed. - The case of assigning the work of various units of the association was resolved to be drafted by the chairman and submitted to the next general meeting for approval. - The date of the next meeting of the preparatory committee was resolved to be held next Monday (the 18th) at the People's Education Hall.

Exhibition Committee. - The funds of this association, in addition to the appropriation from the Municipal Government, are raised by the participating groups and institutions. - This charter shall be implemented after being passed by the General Assembly of Representatives. - This charter may be amended if there are any matters that are not covered.

Plan Outline

The full text of the Shanghai 15th Health Movement Plan Outline states, "The 15th Shanghai Health Movement is a continuation of the previous 14th Health Movement. Therefore, its work should continue the past and usher in the future, connecting with the previous session and laying the groundwork for the future. The matters held in the 14th Health Movement should be continued, taking into account current needs, while on the other hand, a new focus of work should be selected as the characteristics and trends of this Health Movement. The National Government has issued a Children's Year from August 24th to July 25th of the following year. This Health Movement coincides with this event and is held during the implementation period of Children's Year. Therefore, children are the main target of its activities, and the dissemination of parental health knowledge is secondary, in order to achieve a mutually beneficial effect and spread health knowledge in ordinary families. This is in terms of the specific principles of this Health Movement. If measured by facts, this Health Movement, in addition to inheriting past work, also bears the mission of enlightening children's health and imparting family health knowledge. Therefore, its complexity and scope are even greater than those of previous Health Movements. However, as such, the expenses are inevitably huge. At a time when the city is exhausted and the social and economic conditions are difficult, it is not realistic to allow this Health Movement to spend too much. Therefore, there must be some changes in the methods, that is, to earnestly contact and cooperate with cooperating institutions or groups, in order to obtain the union and assistance in terms of material, spiritual, and work, and to reduce a part of the burden of this Health Movement. The matters of inheritance and the work of creation are divided into two major categories, which are described as follows: A. Matters of inheritance, 1. General health propaganda: 1. Select a suitable location to hold a grand exhibition for 10 to 20 days, to display various propaganda materials related to health, such as models, specimens, magazines, books, instruments, hanging pictures, tables, photos, etc. These exhibits should be widely collected in advance, so that the arrangement can be unhurried, orderly, and avoid duplication, and easy to manage. It can give the audience a systematic and profound impression, and it is hoped that they will understand the structure of the human body and the causes of diseases, and know what to be alert to after the meeting, and pay attention to maternal and infant health. 2. Major newspapers publish a special issue one day, publishing health propaganda texts. 3. Distribute slogans and leaflets by plane. 4. Paste slogans on streets, playgrounds, trams, and buses. 5. Invite the mayor and celebrities to broadcast speeches on the city's radio station. 6. Ask the Social Affairs Bureau to order the city's entertainment groups to sing or broadcast health songs and plays (the plays are supplied by the association, or handed over to the Social Affairs Bureau for review by this bureau). 7. Formulate fixed enamel slogans (can be negotiated to donate some according to their ability). 2. Free vaccination against cholera, typhoid fever, and dysentery mixed vaccine is provided to citizens for large-scale mixed vaccine vaccination. 3. Cleanliness movement. 1. Hold a city-wide clean-up to awaken the public's attention to environmental hygiene and street cleanliness. 2. Continue to hold kitchen competitions. B. Original work. 1. Infant health competition. 2. Children's health speech competition. 3. Children's health drawing competition. 4. Children's health clothing show. 5. Mothers, although this Health Movement has the above-mentioned increase in original work, its funding will not be difficult because of this. It is good to invite cooperation from all parties according to the above reasons, so that spiritual and material pity can be obtained.

The Robbers in the Fish Bank Giant Robbery Case Are Found to Have Committed Another Robbery Case, and the Special Court Continues to Question Them Yesterday, the Robbers' Confessions Are Evasive 125

The Tongrenchang Fish Bank on Xiaodongmen Street in the French Concession was robbed of a huge sum of money on the morning of the 10th of last month. Later, Inspector Jin Lilin, translator Li Xianyang, detectives Zhang Ziying, Qin Youyu, Tian Shiqing, detective Ma Yizhi, and others of the French Concession Police Station solved the case and arrested the robbers He Zhangsheng, also known as Xiao Mujian (31 years old, from Shaoxing), Fan Ada (28 years old, from Jiangyin), Dai Xiaosizi, also known as Yifa (31 years old, from Yancheng), Chen Xiaoerzi (28 years old, from Qingjiang), and the woman He Chen (28 years old, from Suzhou, her husband is He Qing'en, who is a dismissed Public Concession detective, recently arrested for theft and sentenced to seven years and six months by the First Special Court), and more than ten suspected accomplices. Stolen money of 1,298 yuan and several real and fake pistols were seized. After interrogation by the Special Court, the suspected accomplices who were not related to the case were released first, and He and others were remanded in custody for further verification of the situation at a later date, as reported previously. It is now known that the main culprit in the case, Qiu Bainian (from Ningbo), was an apprentice at the Baokang Qianzhuang at 505 Sichuan Road. He stopped working four years ago. Qiu knew about the relationship between Tongrenchang Fish Bank and Baokang Qianzhuang when he was at the bank, and he knew the details, so he colluded with He Zhangsheng, Fan Ali, and the fugitive Lao Pan and others to plan the robbery. After Qiu divided the stolen money, he deposited 1,000 yuan into the Bank of China. Two days later, he withdrew 990 yuan, leaving only 10 yuan. The deposit book has now been seized by the French Concession Police Station. However, Qiu fled without a trace and has not been captured. Yesterday morning, Judge Li Changnian of the Second Special Court came to the Criminal Court and ordered the arrested criminals to be brought in for further interrogation, and instructed lawyer Jin Xiongbo to defend the defendants. First, lawyer Yuan Jiahong of the Police Station stated the facts of the case, and said that it had been found that the first defendant, He Zhangsheng, had colluded with others on March 6 this year to rob Qin Jichen's house at 26 Zhizhong Lane, West Zilaishui Street, of more than 1,000 gold, and that the defendant Dai Xiaojiaozi had also committed the crime of receiving stolen goods, which was the robbery case in Yideli Lane, Lao Beidou Street. The defendants committed the crime of robbery with a gang of three or more people, and it is requested that they be punished in accordance with Article 330 of the Criminal Law, etc. When asked, He Zhangsheng confessed that he was invited by the fugitive Qiu Bainian to involve Fan Ada and the fugitive Lao Pan and others in the robbery. There was a pistol, which was borrowed by He Chen from Chen Xiaoerzi through Xiao Sizi. Afterwards, he gave them 720 yuan, and the civilians got 1,050 yuan, which was the stolen money seized in the case. He Chen confessed to lending the pistol, but did not dare to help with the robbery. Fan Ada confessed to helping with the robbery and got more than 500 yuan. Dai Xiaosizi confessed to borrowing the pistol from Chen Xiaoerzi on behalf of others. Chen Xiaoerzi said that the pistol was borrowed from a Geng surnamed person by a civilian, and he got 500 yuan afterwards. I got ten yuan. At first, I only knew about fighting, but I didn't know about robbery. The rest of the words were evasive. The court verified the confessions and ordered that they be interrogated again on the 19th. The defendants were still remanded in custody.

Youxin Coal Company Undertakes Sales, Judgment in the Liujiang Coal Lawsuit, Shen Jinzhou Found Not Guilty of Defamation 127

Youxin Coal Company claimed that Zhang Yanzhang, because of violating the resolutions of the joint meeting of executive and supervisory committees of the Coal Industry Association, refused to undertake the sale of products from the Liujiang Coal Mine illegally seized by the pseudo-autonomous region of eastern Hebei, and privately entered a large amount of Liujiang coal and sold it at a lower price. The Liujiang Company reported it to the association, and the association decided to notify the industry to break off economic relations with him. After Zhang Yanzhang of Youxin Company was sanctioned by the assembly, he filed a criminal lawsuit with the District Court of the First Special District against the chairman of the association Liu Hongsheng, standing committee members Mao Chunpu and Pan Yisan, executive committee members Chen Yutang and Wei Hongwen, and Liujiang manager Shen Jinzhou for defamation. Liu and others also hired lawyers Xu Shihao and Zuo Dedao to defend them. After repeated summons by the court, the Coal Industry Association submitted all the relevant documents of the association's punishment of Youxin Company and other industries for violating the resolution and privately selling the stolen Liujiang coal that had been seized, in order to prove that Zhang Yanzhang was only seeking private gain and disregarded public opinion. Zhang began to realize that he had become the target of public criticism, so at the beginning of the debate, he applied to withdraw the self-suit against all the defendants except Shen Jinzhou. The court approved the request. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye held another court session and ruled that the main text of the judgment against Shen Jinzhou stated that Shen Jinzhou was not guilty. This case has been valued by the entire coal industry since it occurred. Whenever there was a court hearing, many people in the industry went to listen. Now it can be regarded as the end of a stage.

Car Drives into Huangpu River: Eight People Tragically Drown; Only Three Bodies Recovered as of Last Night; Cause of Accident Suspected to be Driver's Unfamiliarity with Route 128

Yesterday morning around 2:00 AM, Yu Run Trading Company at No. 16 Xiaodongmen Main Street and Tong Ren Chang Trading Company at No. 13 dispatched employees Ye Shuping, Gu Cangsu, along with employees who were also brokers Dong Ziyuan, Gu Junchen, Chen Shengshan, Wang Yongkui, and Hu Jinglian. Together, they hired a car with Shanghai French Concession license plate No. 6835, owned by Wu Zhuofei of Xiaodongmen, to go to Dinghai Island. The car was driven by Wu's driver, named A Mao. Unexpectedly, at around 4:40 AM, the Yangshupu Police Station received a report from residents on Liping Road, stating that a car had suddenly been discovered floating on the water surface near the shore and requesting investigation. After receiving the information, the police station immediately dispatched detectives. They confirmed that there was indeed a car floating on the water surface, with license plate No. 6835. However, there were no passengers in the car, and the driver was also missing. It was concluded that they must have sunk to the bottom. Immediately, water ghosts and boatmen were hired to search and salvage the bodies. Soon, two bodies were recovered, but their identities were unknown. After repeated inquiries, the faces of the two bodies were identified as Ye Shuping, an employee of Yu Run Trading Company, and Hu Jinglian. The other five people and the driver were still missing. As the current was very strong at the time, it was unknown whether they had drifted elsewhere. Detectives then summoned ambulances and first transported the two bodies to the hospital for examination before sending them to the mortuary. Meanwhile, efforts were made to raise the floating car ashore. Before long, Sun Guchen, the owner of Tong Ren Chang Trading Company, and relatives and friends of the victims also received the tragic news. In the misty rain at dawn, they drove to the scene, weeping bitterly by the river, a heartrending sight. Sun Guchen personally requested the police station to continue sending water ghosts to search for the remaining six bodies on the spot. By that night, the body of Gu Cangsu was recovered, but the whereabouts of the others were still unknown. Among the eight victims, only Ye Shuping was from Jiashan, 37 years old. The other six were all from Pudong. According to various speculations, the cause of the accident was likely due to the driver, A Mao, being unfamiliar with the route at the time. The police station is still investigating the matter, while Yu Run and Tong Ren Chang are handling the aftermath. Pig merchants view this as a dangerous route, leading to a decrease in sources.

Piracy Rampant: Pig Boats Robbed Again; Pig Merchants View it as a Dangerous Route, Leading to a Decrease in Sources 129

The Jiangbei pig boat Jin Heli, carrying 238 live pigs from Sun Yuanji Pig Company to Shanghai for sale, was sailing on the Qixu Port sea area at approximately 1:00 AM on the 9th of this month when a Chongming boat sailed towards it. Inside the boat were 17 or 18 pirates armed with several rifles and two Mauser pistols. They fired a warning shot and ordered the boat to stop. The pirates then swarmed aboard, locked the crew and pig merchants in the cabin, and began looting 92 live pigs, 10 legal tender dollars, clothing, bedding, oil, and rice. Before leaving, they also destroyed the boat's sailing equipment. The pirate boat then sailed north. The pig boat arrived in Wusong yesterday, where the experienced foreman reported the incident to the Shanghai Pig Industry Association's Wusong office. The office then requested the Third District Water Police to investigate and apprehend the criminals and recover the stolen goods. It is reported that the Pig Industry Association held a meeting because pig boats have been repeatedly robbed this year, but the authorities have not solved a single case, leading to more rampant piracy. Pig merchants view this as a dangerous route. If effective protection measures are not taken quickly, it will affect business and have significant consequences. After discussion, it was decided to send a letter to the Third District Water Police requesting a strict investigation of the pirates' whereabouts and to submit a petition to the municipal government requesting effective protection measures to safeguard the pig industry and facilitate shipping.

Lili Company Sues Cai Shengbai; Trial Concluded; Whether It Constitutes Defamation is the Focus of Dispute; Defense by Both Parties Concludes Investigation 130

Since the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs started organizing group weddings, it has felt that the attire of the brides and grooms during the wedding ceremony was quite inconsistent, making it insufficient to create a grand spectacle and contradicting the purpose of the New Life Movement's "uniformity." Therefore, it specially designated Kaili Silk and Satin Company, established by the Meiya Silk Weaving Factory on Jing'an Temple Road, to exclusively produce the group wedding attire, in order to show uniformity. After the group wedding was promoted and implemented by the Bureau of Social Affairs, other legal entities also followed suit, and the sales of wedding attire soared. Lili Standard Silk and Satin Company, located next to Kaili, published an advertisement in the newspaper in October of last year, stating that it would provide free production of Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs-approved blue robe and black jacket standard wedding attire. At that time, Kaili believed that since it had been designated by the Bureau of Social Affairs to produce the attire first, Lili should not imitate its name and filed a petition with the Bureau of Social Affairs requesting a prompt cessation. Subsequently, the bureau issued an instruction to warn Lili Company. Therefore, Kaili posted the instruction in its window and added the words "When purchasing Meiya standard wedding attire, please beware of imitation and inferior goods" to the instruction. Lili's manager, Lin Zhixiang, saw this and believed that Kaili's actions publicly damaged Lili's reputation. Therefore, he hired a lawyer to file a criminal self-accusation against Cai Shengbai, the general manager of Meiya, and Gao Shiheng, the deputy general manager and manager of Kaili, in the First Special District Local Court, requesting punishment according to law, and attaching a civil suit requesting the defendant to publish an apology in the newspaper. During the first court hearing, the defendants were not all present, so the hearing was postponed until the afternoon before yesterday. Judge Yang Qianchang interrogated the defendants again. Both Cai and Gao appeared in court with their defense lawyer, Chen Churu. During the hearing, both parties did not dispute the fact that the defendant's company posted the Bureau of Social Affairs' instruction and added the words "beware of imitation" to the instruction paper. What needed to be investigated was whether these actions constituted the crime of defamation. The lawyers from both sides then debated the point. The plaintiff's lawyers, Xue Jiaqi and others, stated that the defendant's actions constituted deliberate defamation and requested the court to rule in accordance with the plaintiff's claims. The defendant's lawyers argued that the Bureau of Social Affairs' instruction was equivalent to a trademark registration document, and companies and shops commonly displayed trademark registration documents in their stores. Therefore, the defendant's display of the instruction was not illegal, and the added words "beware of imitation" did not specifically refer to the plaintiff. Therefore, since the documents were not forged and the defamation was unfounded, the court should declare the defendants innocent. Judge Yang then ordered both parties to withdraw and await the verdict next Monday.

Stealing American Soldier's Diamond Ring: Lihua Silver Shop Accused of Receiving Stolen Goods 133

Also Discovering Impersonation and Abetment; Wang Chuandong and Two Others Released on Bail Pending Judgment

Yan Zhaofa and Zhang Heshang, who worked as waiters at the No. 4 Detachment of the U.S. Marine Corps barracks on Chengdu Road, conspired on the night of April 21 to steal a diamond ring worth 1,500 yuan belonging to the head of the detachment. The next day, they took it to Lihua Silver Shop at No. 120 Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, to inquire about the value and authenticity of the diamond ring. Wang Chuandong, the shop owner from Nanjing, and Dong Songnian, a partner from Shaoxing, examined the ring and determined that it was only worth eight yuan. Yan and Zhang felt that the value was too low, so they took it away and pawned it at Yuanfeng Pawnshop on Xin Zha Road for 50 national currency dollars. They then returned to Lihua Silver Shop and stated that they had pawned it for 50 yuan, and showed the pawn ticket. Wang Chuandong and Dong Songnian immediately offered 18 yuan to buy the pawn ticket. Wang then sent Wu Zhongyuan from Suzhou to Yuanfeng Pawnshop to redeem the diamond ring. Later, the Xin Zha Police Station discovered the case. Chinese detective Ding Huaguo arrested the two thieves, Yan and Zhang, and sent them to the First Special Court. After interrogation, in addition to punishing the thieves, the police determined that Wang Chuandong, the owner of Lihua Silver Shop, his partner Dong Songnian, and Wu Zhongyuan were suspected of conspiring to receive stolen goods. The police station filed charges according to the law. The Special Court once summoned them for questioning. Wang and Wu claimed to be ill and did not appear. Only Dong Songnian appeared in court, but Dong concealed his own name and impersonated Wang Chuandong. After Judge Ye Shengchao discovered this, he believed that Dong had impersonated someone and ordered the case to be postponed. Dong Songnian was ordered to be handed over to the police station for investigation. The police station concluded its investigation, determining that Dong Songnian not only had impersonated someone, but Wang Chuandong also had abetted the crime. Therefore, yesterday morning, when Judge Ye continued the hearing of the case, police lawyer Qian Xunjiu, in addition to charging Wang, Dong, and Zhang with the crime of receiving stolen goods in accordance with Article 349, Section 3 of the Criminal Law, also charged Wang and Dong with the crimes of abetment and concealment of fugitives in accordance with Article 29 and Article 164, Section 2 of the Criminal Law. He then stated the above circumstances and requested a verdict according to law. Wang Chuandong confessed to buying the pawn ticket for 18 yuan and sending Wu Zhongyuan to Yuanfeng Pawnshop to redeem the ring. However, the person who came to sell the ring was wearing Western clothes and claimed that the diamond ring was bought for 120 yuan and now wanted to sell it. Wang said that Lihua Silver Shop specialized in redeeming pawn tickets, so he offered eight yuan for the gold in the ring. As for the diamond, he did not know its authenticity, so he let the person take it away. But the deal did not go through. Later, the man in Western clothes came back, so he offered 18 yuan to buy the pawn ticket. He said that he was sick during the previous hearing, so he had Dong Songnian represent him. Dong and Wu confessed to the same events. After the defendant's lawyer rose to defend, the court ordered Wang Chuandong to pay 3,000 yuan bail, and Dong and Wu to each pay 2,000 yuan bail, to await the verdict next Tuesday.
