Central Bank Inspection Report 139

The 282nd Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Exchange Certificates states that, in accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the amount of exchange certificates issued by the bank and the reserve funds. The 282nd inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of the bank on May 9, 1936. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: A. The total amount of silver dollar exchange certificates issued was 270,192,495 yuan, including 243,646,551 yuan in silver dollar certificates and 26,545,944 yuan in subsidiary currency certificates. The total amount of exchange certificate reserve funds was 270,192,495 yuan, including 185,040,395 yuan in cash reserves. Of this cash reserve, 152,874,867.71 yuan was held in the bank's issuing headquarters, branches, and sub-branches, and 32,165,527.29 yuan was deposited with other banks. The guarantee reserve was equivalent to 85,152,100 yuan in silver dollars. B. The total amount of customs gold exchange certificates issued was 373,324.70 yuan. The total amount of customs gold exchange certificate reserve funds was 373,324.70 yuan. This reserve fund included 7,351.95 taels of gold, which was priced at 50,779 full customs gold, equivalent to 373,324.70 yuan. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60 percent, and the remainder must be guaranteed by legal guarantees. The results of this inspection showed that the cash reserve exceeded 60 percent, and the guarantee reserve was within 40 percent, which is in accordance with the law. This report is hereby issued. May 11, 1936, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun; Supervisors, Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiqu.

Shanghai's Glass Manufacturing Industry - Editor 141

(Excerpts from the Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Overview, Part 24)

Overview – Glass manufacturing was invented in China long ago. However, all production was done by hand, and the technology was very backward. In the 29th year of the Guangxu reign (Qing Dynasty), Su Ren Zhang Jian (also known as Zhang Ji Zhi), Xu Jiu Xiang, and others raised 830,000 taels of silver to establish the modern Yaoxu Glass Factory in Jiangbei. However, due to a lack of experience and poor management, it closed in the 2nd year of the Xuantong reign. Glass factories in Shanghai started a little later than Yaoxu, but have a history of over twenty years. Renhe Glass Factory was established in the first year of the Republic of China (1912). In the fourth year of the Republic of China (1915), Chinese businessmen bought the Japanese-owned Zhonghua Glass Factory and renamed it Zhonghua Fengji Glass Factory. In the ninth and tenth years of the Republic of China (1920-21), the Gongyi Glass Factory and Shanghai Glass Co., Ltd. followed. Subsequently, the Pudong No. 1 Glass Factory, Xiechang Glass Factory, Guangming Electrical Appliances Co., Ltd., and Tonghe Glass Factory were established. The industry flourished in the sixteenth and seventeenth years of the Republic of China (1927-28), with a total of more than thirty companies. After the eighteenth year of the Republic of China (1929), the industry suffered a setback due to the impact of expensive gold and cheap silver. The Shanghai war caused even more severe damage, with Renhe, Zhonghua Fengji, Shanghai, and several other factories being burned down. After the war ended, the industry revived, with new factories such as Yeye, Jinghua, and Zhongyang Chemical emerging, all on a considerable scale. This is a general overview of the evolution of the glass industry in Shanghai.

The types of glass products are numerous, broadly divided into flat glass, optical glass, chemical glassware, and decorative glass. However, most of the glass factories in Shanghai suffer from insufficient capital and lack of precision in their technology. The majority of their products are still made of material, especially daily necessities such as bottles, cups, jars, and lamps. Currently, only Yaohua manufactures flat glass. Therefore, China still relies on imports to supply flat glass, which is something we should distinguish.

The main raw materials for manufacturing glass and material are glass sand, saltpeter, lime, fluorite, manganese powder, soda ash, sulfuric acid, and other substances. The local factories mainly obtain these materials from inland China or overseas. Mineral materials such as glass sand, lime, and fluorite can be supplied from inland China. However, manganese powder relies on the Japanese, and soda ash is mostly produced by Underdown, a British company. Chinese people still have difficulty independently producing this chemical industry raw material. Therefore, in terms of the glass industry, Chinese people still need to work hard to increase production, reduce the import of foreign goods, and further seek self-sufficiency in chemical industry raw materials. Only in this way can we seek the prosperity of the national glass industry.

Imports of Foreign Glass – China still needs to rely on the import of foreign glass products to meet the needs of the domestic market, as mentioned earlier. Now, the import volume, types, and sources will be described one by one for the reference of the Chinese people.

There are many types of imported glass products, among which ordinary window glass sheets account for the largest proportion. Shanghai has the most ports for importing various types of glass, accounting for more than 60% of the total national import volume. Now, according to customs reports, the figures for the past three years are listed below (unit: 1,000 Customs Gold Units):

In terms of countries, the largest importers are Czechoslovakia, Germany, and Belgium. Czechoslovakia is particularly worth mentioning. Czechoslovakia is a small country in Europe that Chinese people have not paid much attention to, but its glass and glass products are quite popular in China. According to Czech statistics, its imports of glassware to China in 1930 were 6.085 thousand crowns (Czech currency), and in 1934 it could still maintain 7.128 thousand crowns, without declining with the general shrinkage of China's import trade, which shows its popularity. The "Inwald" trademark glassware displayed in major stores in Shanghai is produced in Czechoslovakia. Furthermore, the glass utensils in the Paramount Ballroom and the International Hotel also come from Czechoslovakia, which shows the close relationship between Czech glass products and Shanghai's industry and commerce.

Recent Situation of Major Factories in Shanghai – According to the Shanghai Yearbook (1935 edition), there are a total of 78 glass manufacturing factories in China, with 31 in Shanghai. The capital of the whole country is 3,019,000 yuan, and Shanghai accounts for 607,000 yuan. The output of the whole country is 4,992,000, and Shanghai accounts for 3,210,000. Among the 31 factories in Shanghai, 18 have a capital of more than 10,000 yuan, and the remaining 13 have a capital of only more than 1,000 yuan. The situations of the main factories (manufacturing glassware) are described separately below:

1. Zhongyang Chemical Glass Factory – This factory was organized by Xu Xinzhi and others, the former director of Ruihe Crucible Factory. It was established in August 1934 with a paid-up capital of 50,000 yuan. The factory is located at No. 1332 Pingliang Road, covering an area of 2.8 mu. It is a rented land with buildings. There is a large stove in the factory, with new equipment and more than 50 employees. The distribution office was originally in Hua'efang, but this spring it moved to No. 566 Sanma Road due to business development. Its products are mainly medical and chemical glassware, supplemented by household utensils. The factory's products are excellent and have a wide sales network, almost unable to meet the demand. Last year's total turnover reached more than 100,000 yuan, and it may be able to increase by another half in the future.

2. Zhonghua Glass Factory – This factory is solely operated by Zheng Zhonghan with a capital of 30,000 yuan. It was established in July 1932. The factory is located at No. 957 Tangshan Road, specializing in the production of various types of bottles and various glass products. The factory building and base are all its own property. There are three kilns built inside, costing about 3,000 to 4,000 yuan. Various bottle molds are worth about 25,000 to 26,000 yuan. The factory's business is mainly based in Shanghai, and it has connections with various cosmetics manufacturers, candy factories, and wineries. Therefore, its business is quite good. Last year's turnover reached 180,000 yuan, with a profit of 20,000 yuan. (To be continued)

Shen Bao National Goods Special Issue

How to Overcome the "Economic National Crisis"? 142

— Xuan Wan

Only by Developing Domestic Products Can We Revive National Industry

Everyone knows that China is currently experiencing the most severe national crisis, especially the economic crisis. Due to years of dumping of foreign goods, the surge in import surpluses, and the rolling outflow of huge amounts of foreign exchange every year, rural areas have gone bankrupt, industry and commerce have declined, and the tide of recession has swept the country. The weakness of the purchasing power of the majority of the people has reached its extreme. The collapse of the entire national economy has entered the final stage, and how to overcome the economic national crisis has become the most urgent and important issue for workers today. The future survival of the people of the whole country is only tied to overcoming the economic national crisis.

However, the painful fact tells us that until recently, the "economic national crisis" has not been eased due to the growing decline of our national livelihood. On the contrary, it has become more serious recently due to the intensified aggression of foreign forces. The rampant smuggling in North China and South China, and the Northwest market, after the completion of the highway, the domestic goods industry was about to develop, but foreign goods took the lead and dumped them on a large scale, which greatly affected the sales of domestic goods industry. In particular, the presence of smuggled goods everywhere not only leaves no room for domestic goods, but also affects the difficulty of collecting accounts receivable and the return of inventory. It simply whips the domestic goods industry to the point where there is no way to go.

Therefore, we can know that to overcome the economic national crisis, we can only develop domestic products. The specific implementation of developing domestic products is not effective by empty slogans. We must have a clear understanding of the truth of the economic national crisis and its main causes. Then we can prescribe the right medicine, remove the obstacles that prevent the progress of domestic goods, especially prevent smuggling, and expel all kinds of foreign economic oppression. All sovereignty must be independent before we can overcome the economic national crisis and solve the problem of domestic goods development.

Therefore, we must recognize that the development and prosperity of the entire industrial and commercial sector is being shackled and restricted by the economic national crisis. Our future way out must be to break free from these shackles and remove these fetters before we can restore our economic freedom.

At present, our economic national crisis is indeed serious. But we must not be pessimistic or discouraged. We demand national survival, so we must overcome the economic national crisis. To overcome the economic national crisis, we must develop domestic products and revive national industry. The government and the people must work together, unite and work together to achieve our final goal and victory.

Contribution

The Relationship between the Women's World and Domestic Goods 143

— Yang An

The other day, the Shanghai National Goods Movement Federation entertained the ladies of the Shanghai Women's Association and received enthusiastic support from leaders in the women's world. The reports in the newspapers that day were slightly different. As a reporter who participated in the entertainment, the conversation was very satisfactory. I dare to describe the opinions of the women's world and the expectations of the reporter as a notification to comrades who are concerned about the cause of domestic goods:

Leaders in the women's world believe that the progress of domestic goods in recent years is commendable. If the women's world can use domestic goods for their needs in clothing, food, housing, and use, they will do their best to use them. They also said that their clothing is uniformly made of domestic silk and satin, and Cai Junsheng of Meiya was present to confirm it. They also said that children's clothing is made of domestic fabrics, and Sanyou Hongxin is their main customer. They also said that children love their country from the bottom of their hearts and are influenced by education. If parents are careless and buy non-domestic silk and satin, they will declare to their parents that they do not want to wear them. From this point alone, the future of China is very promising. One of the speeches by Mrs. Hua encouraged domestic goods manufacturers to work hard to improve their products so that the women's world would rely on domestic goods for all their clothing, food, housing, and use. She also hoped that they would come up with their own ideas, preserve the inherent beauty of China, and not compete in Westernization and imitate irrelevant patterns. Her words were earnest and sincere, and the domestic goods industry should follow them faithfully. Here, the reporter has three thoughts:

The general women's world has shifted its atmosphere and unanimously tends to buy domestic goods. Therefore, anyone who calls themselves a domestic goods company will be like a marketplace, which is a satisfactory effect of promoting domestic goods for ten years.

The heart of children to love and use domestic goods, in addition to the power of family education, plus the power of school education, its momentum is even greater and stronger. When these people grow up to be masters and housewives, their enthusiasm for using domestic goods is really unstoppable.

The domestic goods industry is the manufacturer, and the women's world is the user. If the manufacturing and user parties can be open and honest, and often contact each other to create an atmosphere of harmony, and often exchange opinions and communicate feelings, then the development of the domestic goods industry cannot be described in words.

If everything can be met with sincerity and discussed with sincerity, then any estrangement can be eliminated. Since the women's world can sincerely support domestic goods and promote domestic goods so much, then even if there are one or two points of difference in consciousness or misunderstandings by intermediaries, do not hold grudges in your heart, so as not to discourage a piece of enthusiasm. The reporter met with Ms. Li Zhenhua, Wang Ruizhu, and Ouyang Jun yesterday, and they spoke highly of the importance of the women's world promoting domestic goods, which is to unite female comrades to engage in the women's world using domestic goods movement. All parties have the same mentality and feel the same need. Although the methods are different, they all lead to the same goal, with the aim of developing domestic goods and eliminating import surpluses. This is a very good phenomenon in the domestic goods industry.

A Short Account of Visiting the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Factory to Manufacture National Party Flags 144

— Tian Ran

On May 7th, the General Bureau for the Production and Sale of Party and National Flags invited people from all walks of life to visit the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Factory to see how the Party and National Flags are manufactured. I went to the factory with Mr. Xu Caicheng and Mr. Ren Jinping for a visit, which took two hours to complete the work of spinning, weaving, dyeing, and finishing. The factory is divided into five departments: The first is the spinning department, which spins cotton into cotton yarn. It has machines for blending cotton, unpacking, transporting cotton, opening cotton, cleaning cotton, carding cotton, drawing cotton, roving, and spinning. There are fifty-two Toyoda-style spinning frames with 15,000 spindles. The scale is very large. The second is the weaving department, which weaves cotton yarn into cloth. The weaving machines are all Toyoda-style, which are highly efficient and can produce more than 3,000 bolts of cloth per day. The third is the bleaching department, which bleaches the cloth. There are more than ten bleaching machines, which are very beautiful and durable. The fourth is the dyeing department, which first dyes the bleached cloth with a base color. The fifth is the printing department, which officially prints the dyed cloth into the colors of the Party and National Flags, and then washes it with steam and water to clean it, and then uses finishing work to make the color bright and the cloth flat. All the raw materials in the factory, except for some pigments, are all domestic raw materials. Mr. Xu has a wealth of experience in the textile industry and gave instructions one by one. He gave detailed instructions on the work of winding yarn, warping yarn, sizing yarn, beaming, drawing-in, and inserting weft. The equipment in the printing department is even more ingenious. According to Mr. Xu, the efficiency of Toyoda spinning machines is 30% higher than that of American machines and 10% higher than that of British machines. It is believable that the Japanese have gone from imitation to creation. There are about 1,300 workers, who are very energetic. Within ten hours, they can print 15,000 yards of Party and National Flags. The daily production can be 200,000 flags if they are No. 1 to No. 3 flags, 80,000 flags if they are No. 4 flags. If they are No. 5 and No. 6 flags, they can produce more than 10,000 flags. The flags of No. 7, No. 8, No. 9, and No. 4 are all around several thousand. The machines used are the fastest and most efficient, so the production is particularly high and the management is flexible. According to statistics, each Party and National Flag goes through 46 processes from cotton to flying in the air. Mr. Zhang Zilian said that this Party and National Flag has three characteristics: It never fades, It is a whole piece of fabric, and It is made of domestic raw materials. My colleagues and I were very satisfied after visiting and took notes.

New Uses for Tung Oil 145

— Sun Linchang

Tung oil is a special product of China, and there are names such as Sichuan Tung, Zheng Tung, and Zhejiang Tung, which are distinguished by their place of origin. Chinese people mostly use it to decorate houses and utensils and to paint ships. Because tung oil has the function of resisting rain and water seepage, general ships are soaked in water all year round. Without the protection of tung oil paint, they are very easy to rot. As for exporting it to foreign countries, it was mostly used in industrial products in the past, and later it also occupied an important position in military products. For example, the exteriors of airplanes and submarines must be lubricated with tung oil to be considered strong. Unexpectedly, in recent years, foreigners have discovered a special use for this substance in the military. Because soldiers on the front line, after each bullet is fired, the barrel of the gun will heat up. If you want to continue to use it, the heat will not dissipate in a moment, which will affect shooting. If you apply tung oil, you can avoid this problem. Recently, the world situation has become increasingly tense, and countries are preparing for war very urgently. Therefore, the export of tung oil from China has increased sharply, and in the past two days, it has occupied the first place in export goods.

Olympic Bell Already Suspended Atop the Stadium Tower 149

(Havas Agency, Berlin, 11th) The government recently cast a large bell for the Olympic stadium, which was suspended this morning atop the stadium gate tower (tower height 76 meters). This bell is made of 14,000 kilograms of pure steel, with a diameter of 2.80 meters and a height of 2.70 meters. One side is cast with a giant eagle, its claws holding an athlete, and the other side is cast with the Brandenburg Gate and a chariot drawn by four horses. When the 11th Olympic World Games open on August 1st of this year, this giant bell will be rung to symbolize the call to gather the youth.

Educational News

The Education of Northeastern China Has Already Been Enslaved; The Puppet Organization Implements Heinous Methods 158

(Central News Agency) According to travelers newly arrived from the Northeast, regarding the general situation of education in the Northeast under the rule of the puppet organization, the following is recorded:

Educational Administration and School Organization

The highest educational administrative organ of the puppet organization is the Ministry of Education and Culture, which has one Secretary-General and one Vice-Minister. It is divided into three divisions: General Affairs, Academic Affairs, and Etiquette. The heads of the General Affairs and Academic Affairs divisions are filled by certain Japanese individuals. The General Affairs Division has four sections: Secretariat, Investigation, General Affairs, and Documentation. The Academic Affairs Division is divided into Specialized and General sections. The Etiquette Division has sections for Social Education and Religion. Additionally, there is an Editorial Committee and Inspectors. In each provincial Department of Education, there is a Director, with divisions below including General Affairs, Science, Academic Affairs, Etiquette, and Inspectorate. The Academic Affairs Division is further divided into School Education and Social Education sections. The section chiefs of General Affairs, Academic Affairs, and the Inspectorate are all certain Japanese individuals. Inspectors and staff members are a mix of certain Japanese individuals and Chinese. Each secondary school has one Principal and one Director for each of the following: Academic Affairs, Discipline, General Affairs, Health, Library, Dormitory Affairs, and Grade Level. The Directors of Academic Affairs and General Affairs are certain Japanese individuals. Recently, many Discipline Directors have also been filled by certain Japanese individuals. The principals of each experimental middle school are also certain Japanese individuals. Each elementary school has an additional Vice-Principal, who is a certain Japanese individual.

For any important instructions to various schools, the Department of Education has the relevant Japanese section chief summon the relevant Japanese director of each school to personally impart the necessary information. If schools have any requests for the Department of Education, the relevant Japanese director directly discusses it with the relevant Japanese section chief or the Director of the Department. The Director and Principal sign and stamp the documents. For matters of confidentiality, even the signing and endorsement procedures are omitted. The relationship between the Ministry of Education and Culture and the Department of Education is the same. All supplies for the schools are distributed by the Department of Education, and the hiring and firing of teachers and staff are also decided by the Department of Education.

Educational Goals

The educational goal of the puppet organization is "loyalty to the monarch and forbearance" for boys' schools, and "virtuous mothers and good wives" for girls' schools. For both boys' and girls' schools, the common goals are to understand the spirit of nation-building, realize Wangdao (the Way of the Benevolent King), and promote amity between the puppet state and certain Japanese individuals and mutual coexistence and co-prosperity.

Schools at All Levels

According to the above-mentioned educational goals, all colleges and universities in the Northeast from before the September 18th Incident are naturally abolished, and middle schools and demonstration schools are also abolished or merged. Vocational schools are reorganized so that the highest aspiration of the general Northeast youth is to be trained as lower-level technicians. Kindergartens and elementary schools are actively expanded because instilling pro-certain Japanese individuals ideas and enslaving the youth are considered most thorough when starting from kindergarten and elementary school. Citizen Party Ideology is eliminated from schools at all levels and replaced with ethics. The number of hours for English and mathematics is reduced, while the teaching of certain Japanese language is increased. Failing certain Japanese language results in failing the grade. History and geography textbooks in middle schools use newly compiled puppet state history and puppet state geography. Other subjects use old textbooks with deletions and alterations. Elementary school textbooks now all use newly compiled ones. Certain Japanese language classes in all schools are taught by certain Japanese individuals. The Department of Education also hires many Japanese teachers for various subjects to serve as instructors in each county. In addition to extolling the amity between the puppet state and certain Japanese individuals, mutual coexistence and co-prosperity, and the true meaning of Wangdao and nation-building, the following training methods are implemented in the discipline of all levels of schools: (A) Singing the national anthem and paying respects to the Imperial Palace: During morning exercises each month, the students and teachers first raise the puppet state flag and sing the puppet state national anthem, and then pay respects to the puppet state Imperial Palace. (B) Viewing the Imperial Portrait and Reading the Imperial Rescript: In the auditorium of each school, a photograph of the rebellious Pu Yi is hung, referred to as the "Imperial Portrait," and two types of "Imperial Rescripts" are treasured: one is the enthronement rescript, and the other is the rescript on a visit to certain Japanese individuals. The content is the golden rule that the "puppet state and certain Japanese individuals are inseparable," instructing all subjects to thoroughly understand, comply with, and follow the order. At all important ceremonies or meetings, the Imperial Portrait must be respected first, and the "Imperial Rescript" must be read aloud. (C) Imperial Rescript Writing Contest: To arouse students' attention to the Imperial Rescript, an Imperial Rescript writing contest is held for all students in "Manchukuo." Each school selects ten students to participate in the preliminary round in the provincial capital. As a result, each school selects two students to go to "Xinjing" to participate in the final round. (D) Organizing Nation-Building Propaganda Teams and Appeasement Teams: To popularize the theory of amity, coexistence, and co-prosperity and deeply root it in the hearts of the people of the puppet "Manchukuo," Nation-Building Propaganda Teams and Appeasement Teams are organized to give lectures on Wangdao, the Concordance Policy, and the essential points of the inseparability of the puppet state and certain Japanese individuals in various places and schools. (E) Honoring Confucius: In provinces and counties with Confucian temples, efforts are made to repair the Confucian temples. In places without Confucian temples, proposals are made to build them, using Confucius's Great Harmony doctrine and the ideas of ruler-ruler and subject-subject to seduce the youth and make them loyal to the puppet organization. (F) Soliciting Paintings to Promote National Conditions: In order to enable the general public to understand the political situation of the puppet organization and foster their awareness of the puppet state, the Jilin Department of Education issued a notice to teachers, staff, and students of all schools last autumn to solicit paintings to promote national conditions.

Policy on Studying Abroad

For students from the Northeast who went abroad before the September 18th Incident with government funding to study in Europe and the United States, the certain Japanese legations and consulates in the host countries reissued tuition fees and advised them to return to their home country. Those who complied were given travel expenses to return home, otherwise, the tuition fees were discontinued. Afterwards, no students were sent to Europe or the United States. Those who wished to pursue further studies were only allowed to study in certain Japanese individuals. Examinations for studying in certain Japanese individuals were divided into the following categories: (A) Selecting middle school teachers to study for one year, with a monthly allowance of 60 yuan. (B) Selecting high school graduates, with monthly tuition ranging from 20 to 50 yuan, depending on the level of the school they entered and the location of their family. (C) Selecting junior high school students. The puppet ambassador to certain Japanese individuals, Ding Shiyuan, suggested that students who are a little older have firm ideas that are not easily assimilated, which hinders the work of concordance between the puppet state and certain Japanese individuals. Therefore, he suggested that students under the age of fifteen be selected to study in certain Japanese individuals. This proposal was adopted, so recently there have been many students from outside the customs around the age of fifteen studying in certain Japanese individuals, with a monthly tuition fee of 20 to 25 yuan. (D) Selecting elementary school teachers to visit certain Japanese individuals in batches, to increase their pro-certain Japanese individuals ideas and make them loyal to enslaved education. (E) Ordering the children of puppet officials to study in certain Japanese individuals. In order to control the Northeast students studying in certain Japanese individuals, the old managers of various provinces were abolished, and a school affairs section was added to the puppet embassy in certain Japanese individuals to specialize in matters related to international students. A certain Japanese individual was appointed as the section chief, and students from Kwantung Province (Dalian) and South Manchuria Medical College and South Manchuria Public School were used to organize groups such as the Youth League, the Shenshui Association, and the Hometown Association to monitor the students' actions under the guise of connecting feelings and prevent them from interacting with students from the mainland provinces.

Restricting Students from Entering the Customs

During the summer vacation of the 24th year, the Jilin Provincial Department of Education of the puppet government convened a meeting of parents of students studying inside the customs. The attendees were mostly civil servants. The meeting was called a meeting, but in reality, it forced parents to recall their children studying inside the customs and change to studying in certain Japanese individuals. Except for those who were about to graduate, all others had to comply. In order to implement this policy, the Ministry of Education and Culture of the puppet government planned to change all schools in the country to start in the spring, so that they would not be connected to the entrance examinations of schools inside the customs. Heilongjiang Province has already implemented this starting this spring. Currently, the puppet education departments of various provinces have received instructions to investigate international students and pay special attention to those seeking education inside the customs.

Screening and Training of Teachers

In addition to managing school affairs and training students, the Japanese staff and teachers in various schools in the Northeast also observe the actions and attitudes of Chinese teachers and staff. The Department of Education often asks Chinese teachers and staff with clear minds to write articles or give speeches on the topic of "Impressions of the New Nation" in order to determine the thoughts of each employee and decide whether to keep them. The Ministry of Education and Culture uses winter and summer vacations to conduct examinations and evaluations of primary and secondary school teachers. The most important item in the examination is the "Spirit of Nation-Building," and the remaining subjects are formal. The Ministry of Education and Culture of the puppet government established a teacher training institute in Nanling, Changchun, and selected current teachers and staff from all over the country to study "Spirit of Nation-Building," "Domestic Affairs," "International Relations," and "Economic Education." The first phase of training lasted for three months, from October 1 to the end of December of the 24th year.

Checking Books

In the winter of the 24th year, the Police Department of Heilongjiang Province of the puppet government notified the Department of Education that all publications of public and private schools must be sent to the department for approval before they can be printed, otherwise they would be prohibited from being printed. In various places outside the customs, books related to national justice or national humiliation had long been burned. In the winter of the 23rd year, the chief of the Social Education Section of the Heilongjiang Provincial Department of Education of the puppet government inspected the books in the province's libraries and people's education centers, and all records related to the "spirit of martial valor" were cut out. Reviewing textbooks is the top priority of the puppet government. In addition to the Editorial Committee of the Ministry of Education and Culture, the organs responsible for planning and implementing this include the Certain Manchurian Culture Association of the Ministry of Civil Affairs, the Fengtian Provincial Youth Education Association, and the South Manchuria Education Association, which are also engaged in the editing of textbooks.

Suppressing Schools and Educators Suspected of Anti-Manchu Activities

The Fengtian Provincial Department of Education of the puppet government believed that anti-Manchu elements had infiltrated the Private Shuren Girls' Academy in Dabeiguan and were spreading anti-Manchu ideas. Therefore, it thoroughly investigated schools and private schools in the city. As a result, 11 middle schools, 11 elementary schools, 18 technical schools, 13 language schools, and 65 private schools were closed down. The puppet organization took last November as a period of major inspection. Many residents were severely punished for communicating with people inside the customs, so everyone was in danger. When the patriotic movement of students inside the customs arose, a large-scale literary dragnet was cast, and 17 educators in Jilin Province were arrested, 12 people in the Changchun education community were arrested, and the same was true in Shenyang, Harbin, and Heilongjiang. However, the number of people arrested is unknown, and the whereabouts of all those arrested are unknown.

Higher Education

(A) Datong College, located in Nanling, Changchun, is a training center for puppet government officials. It is directly under the jurisdiction of the General Affairs Office of the State Council. Its purpose is to train good officials. It recruits certain Japanese graduates, students studying in certain Japanese individuals, and puppet government lower-level officials. After completing their training, they are assigned to various agencies. Certain Japanese are given the best treatment, followed by students studying in certain Japanese individuals, and then non-students studying in certain Japanese individuals. (B) Higher Normal School, located in the old site of Jilin University in Jilin City, with Principal Ma Guanbiao, enrolls certain Japanese students. The annual funding is 307,000 yuan. The Nanling training school is located in Nanling and aims to train primary and secondary school teachers. The director is concurrently held by Xu Ru, the Deputy Minister of the puppet Ministry of Education and Culture. It recruits current primary and secondary school teachers, with an annual funding of 87,336 yuan. In addition, there is a newly established National Higher Agricultural School and the former Sino-Russian co-organized Harbin Institute of Technology, a private medical school. (End)

High School Students in Jiangsu Province Who Do Not Participate in the Proficiency Test Will Not Have Their Student Status Recognized by the Department of Education 159

(Zhenjiang Correspondence) Public and private senior middle schools in Jiangsu Province are currently intensifying training. The graduation of third-year students is approaching, and the proficiency test is imminent. For the convenience of students taking the proficiency test, there are flexible measures. I have recorded it in this newspaper. It is now known that the scope of the test questions, the Proficiency Test Committee decided that algebra and trigonometry would be one group, geometry and analytic geometry would be one group, and physics and chemistry would be divided into upper and lower parts. History and geography are divided into Chinese and foreign groups. At least one question must be selected from each group. This year, it will be postponed. It is also heard that students who refuse to participate in the proficiency test under the pretext of training will not have their student status recognized. However, those who instigate opposition to the proficiency test in school or contact other schools will be investigated by the Department of Education and will be punished according to law and will not be tolerated.

Establishment of Zhejiang Library Association 160

The connection between libraries in Zhejiang Province began with the organization of the Hangzhou Library Association in the 13th year of the Republic of China. Although the association did not last long, in recent years, the library associations of the first and second school districts have made efforts to carry it out. The library business in Hangzhou and other places has also become more and more developed. Last year, the two associations and several local library officials jointly prepared and established the "Zhejiang Library Association" at the Provincial Library on April 19. Representatives from county libraries, public education halls, and school libraries in Hangzhou City, Hang County, Yuhang, Xindeng, Jiaxing, Jiashan, Haiyan, Wuxing, Shaoxing, Zan County, Yuhang, Jiande, Jinhua, Dongyang, Zan County, Yongjia, Lishui, and other places, as well as representatives from libraries of Zhejiang University, Zhijiang Aviation, various middle schools, and various institutions in Hangzhou, totaling more than 90 people, joined and attended the meeting. The inaugural meeting was held in the morning. Director Chen of the Provincial Library was elected as the chairman. The Director of Education and the representatives of the Provincial Party Department, and guests from all walks of life, delivered speeches successively. In the afternoon, the first meeting was held, and the articles of association were approved. Chen Xunci, Sun Ming, Pan Ganjian, Sun Yanzhao and other nine people were elected as directors. The association also compiled and printed a volume of the inaugural meeting, which was distributed to members. The board of directors then met on May 1 to discuss many issues, many of which were about the improvement and cooperation of libraries throughout the province. It is said that recently, there are more than 320 public libraries, people's education halls, and school and institutional libraries in Zhejiang Province. The Provincial Library has a collection of 300,000 volumes, and the daily readership, excluding those reading newspapers, is about 750, making it a leader among provincial libraries.

The Basic Principles of National Salvation Education (Continued) - Broadcast Speech by President Dai 168

In the recent dozen or so years, the Prime Minister saw that to build and save the country, it was necessary to have military force. The Prime Minister was determined to create a revolutionary army in order to save the country. In the 13th year of the Republic of China, when the Chinese Kuomintang was reorganized, Mr. Chiang was given the responsibility of building the army and saving the country. He founded the Whampoa Military Academy, which continues to be the Central Military Academy today. Let us see its strength. With this small force, it quelled the domestic chaos in a very short period of time and created the great cause of uniting the country with revolution. Think about how much power it had in the beginning. The first class had only four hundred and several dozen people. The Prime Minister said on that day, "Revolutionary soldiers must be able to fight a hundred men with one." At the time, many people thought the Prime Minister was exaggerating, but when we look at the results, we can see that the Prime Minister's words were not an exaggeration. Comparing the power at that time with the power of the warlords, how could it only be one to a hundred? I am afraid it was one to a thousand. We must know that the revolutionary army is different from the general army. Compared with the army of the late Qing Dynasty and the anti-revolutionary army before, the revolutionary army is not only proficient in both literary and martial arts, but also emphasizes both skills and virtues. It not only studies martial arts and cultivates literature, but also has technology and ideology. Therefore, it can defeat those who have no technology and no ideology, or who focus on one aspect of physics. In the past history of China, it is very clear that the separation of civil and military affairs can be seen, and the harm of the incompatibility of skills and virtues can be seen.

Looking again at modern countries, the reason why they can become rich and strong countries, peaceful countries, and culturally advanced countries is that they clearly focus on methodology and consistent civil and military activities. We must seek national unity from this methodology and consistent civil and military activities, and we must concentrate this power to create a strong force for the country and the nation in the world. This is what we must start from education, that is, to realize the Prime Minister's proposition of "creating organized and powerful citizens and an organized and powerful society." If we follow this direction, we can achieve the four major goals of education: "First, to be filial children at home; second, to be useful talents in society; third, to be loyal citizens in the country; and fourth, to be upright people in the world." In military terms, that is, to make all soldiers in the country receive national education, and all citizens in the country receive sound training, especially military training. We must know that national military training not only creates physically strong citizens, but also creates citizens who abide by order, because saving the country and education is not only in the narrow sense of military affairs, but especially emphasizes the social order and sound organization, so as to create a force. Looking at today's economic construction, if we have a sound organization and a sound training, then any undertaking and any major work can be accomplished. For example, taking the Yellow River in the north, since it left the Longmen, it has been unstable. In the past twenty years, there have often been major floods. In recent years, there have been almost no years without floods. Last year alone, there were dozens of counties and millions of people in Shandong and Jiangsu provinces who were fighting the water on both sides of the Yellow River.

Bonds Rebound Slightly, Market Price Rises by 0.15 to 0.7 Yuan, Transactions Very Light, Many Observers

Yesterday, at the Chinese Securities Exchange, the market rebounded slightly from the continuous decline of the past few days. Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 187

— (Yun Su)

If you are trapped in a heavily guarded prison, you should not be disheartened and weep; nor should you hope that others will come to your aid and rescue you. You should rely on your own strength, fight against the demons of adversity, protest, and declare war, completely shattering and casting off the chains that bind you, restoring your former freedom, and obtaining happiness in life. Otherwise, your suffering will never end.

Whatever one's life may be, it is always better to have some waves and ripples. Regardless of whether they are joyful, painful; happy, tragic; victorious, or unsuccessful, they are much better than being mediocre, silent, obscure, and uneventful. It's like drinking ruby red wine and bitter black water, which are definitely better than drinking plain boiled water.

Love can bring people infinite happiness, but it can also give people infinite wounds. However, the taste of love is definitely not something everyone can experience, nor something everyone can comprehend. Because even if you are close to it and admire it, it may reject you from afar and not develop any passion with you, then you can do nothing about it. I think young friends would be better off dedicating their naked hearts entirely to literature and art. Because as long as you fall in love with it, it will never reject you or tease you, and it can at least give you some comfort and some sweetness.

A Cross-Section of a City Corner 188

— Hua Ling

Between seven and eight o'clock in the evening, the neon lights outside the big stores, red and blue, reflect each other. Under this intense neon light, everything at a crossroads is projected, a cross-section of a city corner.

The red police light turned green, and the cars crowded at the north-south intersection bravely rushed forward. There were big-bottomed ones, snub-nosed ones, old-fashioned three-dimensional ones, and new-fashioned streamlined ones. Carrying, of course, were gentlemen and noble ladies. But behind these cars, there were rickshaw pullers who overestimated their abilities, desperately chasing forward, as if wanting to compete with the cars for speed. -- No, they were running for their livelihood. On their arms, there were always quasi-gentlemen sitting askew in the carriages, pretending to be leisurely, running like cattle and horses.

The trams on the north-south road were also slowly crawling forward. Pedestrians were also rushing forward at this moment, crossing the road. Old Shanghainese always strolled leisurely, so calmly. At this time, under the red police light at the east-west intersection, snake-headed trams stopped again, spitting out a large group of male, female, old, and young passengers, and at the same time swallowing another large group. The platform was followed by a burst of commotion. The children selling evening newspapers were shouting with hoarse voices. Beggars, with forced smiles, were chasing pedestrians. Prostitutes with red rouge and white powder on their faces, wrapped in red and green cheongsams, were constantly sweeping pedestrians with flirtatious eyes. Hooligans were teasing wantonly. Little rascals were staring at the velvet hats of certain passengers in the cars, planning to "snatch the top hat." Everything was extremely active.

The patrolman at the intersection blew his whistle, the color of the police light changed, and trams, cars, rickshaws, and pedestrians were again interweaving on the east-west road. Commotion was being staged again at the north-south intersection. Cars -- people -- cars --, constantly coming and going on the east-west road, the north-south road, always so crowded, pushing, but the shop assistants in the big stores along the street were just idly watching with their sleeves folded, although the neon lights, red and blue, were constantly shining outside the window.

Thoughts on Yu Jianhua's Art Exhibition 189

— Huang Binhong

Among my friends, there are two Yu Jianhuas. One is Yu Jianhua from Taicang, and the other is Yu Jianhua from Jinan. Yu Jianhua from Taicang is a member of the Nanshe Society, and Yu Jianhua from Jinan is a member of the Lanman Society. One is skilled in poetry, ancient prose, and lyrics, and the other is skilled in calligraphy and painting. I once visited Yu Jianhua from Taicang with Yu Jianhua from Jinan on the Double Ninth Festival in the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, and the two Yus then became friends through writing. Now Yu Jianhua from Taicang is ill and disabled at home, while Yu Jianhua from Jinan is showing off his artistic talents on the art scene in Shanghai. Every time he holds an art exhibition, his works are always highly sought after. His learning comes from the school of Chen Shizeng of Yining. Previously, Shizeng lived in Shanghai and established the Wenmei Society with Master Hongyi (namely Li Shutong) of Qingdao, inviting me to join. He gave me a branch of ink plum blossom he wrote himself, Shutong produced seal carvings, Qingdaoren made clerical script, and we talked day and night, which was very enjoyable for a while. Later, we dispersed, Shizeng and Qingdaoren passed away one after another, Shutong converted to Buddhism, and I am also getting old. It seems like looking back at old events. Mr. Yu came to the south, became more skilled, and wrote more works. In recent years, he sailed on the Ou River, climbed Hua Peak, and searched all the wonders of the mountains and rivers of eastern Zhejiang and Jiangxi, presenting them one by one in his brush and ink. He will gather his usual masterpieces and exhibit them for the public to enjoy. I was able to see them and sighed that the achievement of ancient literati in art must be based on reading ten thousand books and traveling ten thousand miles, and then they can broaden their minds, express their emotions, and not share the same likes and dislikes as the customs of the time. Mr. Yu is still young and diligent in his studies. Even now, the works on display, modeling mountains and imitating water, are all exquisite. What he has seen is enough to make those who are old in the literary and art world step back. If Shizeng and other gentlemen were still alive, I don't know how they would praise him happily. Looking back and forth between the past and the present, and observing this gathering, I secretly feel happy for myself. I write this casually in the idle window. May of the Bingzi year of the Republic of China, Huang Binhong, at the age of seventy-three.

From Milk Chicken to People Tired of the City 190

— Fo

There is a family in Tiansizhuang, Suzhou, who raises a cow and a bull, and also has a small disinfection device. Not only can the whole family, men, women, old and young, have fresh milk in the morning and evening all year round, but also relatives and friends let the calves born by the cow be female, and after they grow up, they add a source of milk, and the male ones are slaughtered. The meat of the calves is unusually tender. If the excess milk is used to feed the chickens, when they grow up, they become milk chickens, which are fresh, tender and delicious, incomparable to any meat food. For example, the West Lake Condensed Milk Company in Hangzhou produces light milk in addition to milk powder, condensed milk, butter, and buttermilk, which requires a large amount of milk, so it also buys fresh milk from the people, and the rearing business not only enables it to produce continuously, but also makes people feel happy.

Taking fish farming as an example, its breeding power is very rapid, and raising one hundred fish can feed a family. Why don't people who are tired of the city think about raising animals?

The Phoenix Returns to the Nest 191

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 1 Sipping Tea and Chatting in a Clear Night Window Listening to Rain, Plucking Branches and Admiring the Beauty Shadow Flower Lane Spreads Fragrance

Guoqi's heart was pounding with Bo Bo's. He was thinking, could it be that people knew that he was peeking at them? For a young man to peek at a girl like this, it was inevitable that he would appear frivolous. With a movement in his heart, the blush on his face went straight behind his ears. So he lowered his head and was about to walk away. Just at this moment, he heard the girl gently say, Little brother, pluck a small branch for me. But each of you can only pluck a small branch, don't pluck too much, after all, flowers look better growing on the tree. Guoqi was originally going to leave, but after hearing this, he didn't know why, his footsteps stopped. Therefore, he stopped and didn't leave, and he couldn't help but raise his head. This time, he met her face to face. He just saw her eyes turn, and he lowered his head. He casually smelled the small branch of apricot blossom in his hand, then looked up at the apricot blossoms on the wall again, and then went around the stool the children were using to pick flowers. Because the alley was very narrow, he went around the stool and crossed the dividing line in the middle of the alley. His body and Guoqi's were less than two feet apart. Guoqi felt too close, so he didn't dare to look at her, so he lowered his head again. By the time he raised his head, she had already walked past, but although she had walked past, there was a burst of intoxicating fragrance surrounding his body. When he looked at her, she had already walked away calmly. Although Guoqi was thin-skinned, he didn't feel embarrassed to look at her back, so he stood in the center of the alley and looked in that direction. He thought to himself, she must be walking away like this, and she won't come back. Just as he was watching in a daze, she suddenly stopped and looked back. She probably didn't expect Guoqi to be standing behind her, still looking at her back, so after she turned her head back, she immediately turned around. Guoqi also felt that his attitude was wrong, and his face turned red. But before this embarrassment had completely disappeared, the girl turned her head again. In his imagination, she might have thought that Guoqi wouldn't be standing there for long, so she came back to take a look. Seeing that he was still there the second time, she couldn't look back again, and quickly took two steps and turned around the corner of the alley. This time, Guoqi was stunned, standing in the same place, unable to move. Suddenly, the nine children clapped and laughed, and he was warned in his heart that they must be mocking him here. So he put on a generous appearance and walked forward. He couldn't help but speculate in his heart that this girl was only sixteen or seventeen years old, and seeing her carrying a schoolbag, there was no doubt that she was a female student. Not far from here, there is a girls' middle school, so she must be a female student from this girls' school. Of course, seeing how smart she looked, her homework must be very good. But why didn't she walk with her classmates, but walked alone? That's right, her home must not be far from here, so she walked very calmly. Thinking and walking, he turned into a small alley, and then he raised his head and saw where he was. Ah! This is the alley not far from home, why did he walk back on the road to home? (21)

Local Customs

Parks in Japan 192

— Ji Yun

The most ideal comfort in the monotonous lives of urban people is the park. Our people mostly enjoy themselves alone in private gardens. Therefore, parks in various countries are more common than in our country. There are already more than a dozen parks near Tokyo, Japan, and even more children's parks. Last year, five or six members of a certain elementary school's baseball team were crushed to death by a tram, which was severely criticized by public opinion. Therefore, this year, 157 small parks will be built for children to play and rest. Japanese children throw their schoolbags at home after school and go to the streets and small parks. Five or six-year-old children are often accompanied by their parents, older siblings, and play in the sandpit. There are only trees in the small park, and very few flowers. In the middle are iron exercise equipment, so it is called a children's park.

The temples and shrines in Japan used to have large areas. They were planted with trees and cherry blossoms and arranged as gardens. The larger ones had five-story pagodas, stone lanterns, stone archways and other buildings. Originally, they were used for worship and recreation, but after being transformed and expanded, they became parks. Therefore, foreigners who come to Japan for the first time are always suspicious when they see temples in Japanese parks.

Tokyo's Shiba Park was transformed from Zojoji Temple. The layout is similar to that of our country's gardens. It also uses flying springs and hanging waterfalls to create pools, and stacked stones to create hills, giving it the vitality of mountains and forests. It is an old-fashioned Japanese garden layout method. This kind of park is quiet and winding, but it is not valued by many people, so there are very few visitors. The new parks in our country are also inclined to Westernization, with more lawns, flower beds, and Western-style buildings. The Japanese are the same, such as Hibiya and Ueno Parks, which have all broken away from Japan's inherent Chinese-style gardening method. In fact, our country's gardening method has a unique pleasure.

Japanese parks often have fishing ponds, boating, sports fields, lecture halls, libraries, etc. This can generate some income for expansion and maintenance. In addition to walking, visitors can also get other sports or entertainment. Ueno Park also has science museums, museums, zoos, etc. Using parks to impart knowledge to the public is an excellent method. Each park has various exhibitions every month, such as gardening, bonsai, toys, small animals, etc., which can attract audiences and arouse enthusiasts. In our country's parks, there are tea houses where two or three friends can taste tea and chat, which can also bring a day of peace. In Japanese parks, business is generally not allowed, but there are many street vendors nearby. Therefore, tourists who come to the park bring water bottles and lunch boxes for outdoor picnics. As a result, the park is full of paper scraps and fruit peels, which require several trucks to transport every day.

Utilizing nature is a special feature of Japanese park construction. All lakesides, valleys, and suburban forests are developed into parks. They are connected by very cheap elevated trains. Every spring and autumn, not only does the business of trains greatly increase, but also the people near the park make a lot of profit by selling local products. If our country can slightly organize the scenic spots in various places and connect them with convenient transportation for sightseeing, I think urban people can have more opportunities to contact the countryside and be vigilant. And rural local products can also be revitalized as a result.

Anecdotes

A Page from Li Zhongtang's Diary of Envoy 193

— Fan Xianwei

Li Fuxiang's mission was in March of the twenty-third year of Guangxu. It was originally a special trip to congratulate the Russian Emperor on his coronation. Because Russia had previously hinted to the Qing court that if a minister was sent to congratulate the coronation ceremony, a prince should be specially sent. If not, then Zhongtang would be fine! Therefore, the Qing court specially ordered Zhongtang to go on a mission, and also to tour the major countries of Europe. Zhongtang led his son Jingfang and dozens of attendants and left the country on a certain day in March.

He arrived at Awesisha on April 27 and reached the Russian capital on the 30th.

He was received by the Russian Emperor on May 4. The ceremony was very solemn. On the 18th, he arrived at the Moscow government, where the coronation ceremony was held. After the ceremony, he went to Germany.

He arrived in the German capital on June 13. He visited the German Emperor the next day. He received very good treatment. On the 15th, he visited the retired Prime Minister Bismarck.

He arrived in Paris, the French capital, on July 13. The French government's treatment was no less than that of other countries. After staying for more than ten days, he took a boat from Haarlem to England.

He arrived in England on August 2. England gave Zhongtang a carriage and allowed him to stay at the Duke of Lancashire's residence. The next day, he met the British Emperor at Ashmore Castle and accompanied him to watch the British generals' naval fleet exercises. On the 7th, he was invited to a banquet by the China Association. On the 8th, the British Prime Minister Salisbury asked his wife to host a banquet for Zhongtang at the Prime Minister's residence. On the 10th, he attended a banquet hosted by the Shanghai Hong Kong Bank. Since then, he toured for several days, visiting the Bank of England, the submarine cable engineering bureau, and the shipyard. On the eve of his departure, he went to see the Grand Theater. Arriving in the United States, the United States also treated him with great courtesy. In short, Zhongtang's tour of various countries was regarded as a distinguished guest.

After Zhongtang returned, he first stayed in Tianjin for eleven days, and then went to the capital to report. Suddenly, he was impeached and fined for entering the forbidden garden without permission. Later, he donated ninety taels of silver to redeem his sins.

A Joint Painting of Cihu for Yu Jitiao 194

— Liaoyang

In the year of Ji Chou in Guangxu, I, Yu Zhonglu, Ying Shushen, and Feng Junmu made joint poems at the Shigu Pavilion in Cihu. Han Jun Puquan made this painting for us. Suddenly, fifty years have passed. Shushen and Junmu have already been buried. Zhonglu and I are also getting old. The painting has been transferred to Yu Jun Jitiao. Recently, Jitiao took out the scroll and asked for a poem. Looking back on the past tour, it seems like another world. I wrote four chapters, not knowing where the tears come from.

Opening the scroll, tears flow. Searching for the traces of Ying and Feng here. The green mountains are unharmed, but the poets are old. Only the lake reflects the white hair.

The turquoise mist and light are carefully drawn. The spring rain is Xiao Xiao. The water beside the Fenshi Guan Xiang Shrine. Green to the bridge of the city in the south.

The old garden is dilapidated and there is no home. I feel the years passing by in the poetry arena. Leaving the sentence of Hengbo shining on my eyes. I still dare not face the plum blossoms.

The elegant skirts are fluttering. The rhymes are left to remember the youth. There is still the affectionate Yu Jizi. Willing to protect the flower paper with the remaining ink.

Two days before the Shangsi Festival, Du Liang invited Zhu Bieyou, Chen Liaoshi, Hong Shu'a, Qian Taixi, Wang Zhongxian and other children to a wine gathering. Drinking Bi Chang Liaoshi had a poem that turned out to be even. Liaoyang

The scenery of my hometown is infinite. The sound of orioles enters the orchestra through the trees. The new willows contain smoke and are charming. The remaining plum blossoms dot the water and are beautiful. The windows peep at the thousands of verdant eyebrows. The seats are lined with sages, young and old. It is not easy to enjoy pleasure. How many years will we face each other in a cup?
