Informal Talk

The Hunger Brigade of the Unemployed 207

— Meng Ruo

Recently, a new type of group has been frequently appearing in the world, namely the "Hunger Brigade" organized by the unemployed. Some time ago, a group of workers in Britain, seeing that the authorities were using large sums of money taken from the people to manufacture weapons of mass destruction, while asking a large group of people with no means of livelihood to endure hunger, organized a hunger brigade and petitioned the government, saying: "We demand bread, not warships." Recently, 270,000 unemployed people in New Jersey, USA, also organized a similar group and went to Trenton, with more than a thousand people occupying the inside and outside of the legislature, claiming that they would not withdraw until the legislature had planned relief funds.

Currently, all countries in the world are in a state of economic panic. The increasing number of unemployed people in society has become a serious problem. But are the countries really so poor that they cannot even afford to feed their people? I'm afraid that's not the case. Not to mention anything else, large military expenditures can be paid, so why can't the people's food and clothing be maintained? The demands of the British workers are correct. "We demand bread, not warships." Only bread can solve the hunger of the unemployed, and warships will only increase their suffering. The American workers' application for the authorities to plan relief funds is also a legitimate request.

What is the situation in our country? The organization of the hunger brigade has not yet been seen. However, recently, incidents of poor people抢夺food and farmers riot荒have frequently occurred in various places. This is even more serious than the hunger brigade's organized petition. Last month, a famine riot occurred in Suzhou, which is a reflection of the difficult lives of farmers in general. Recently, the Shanghai Renji Hospital released a report saying: "The number of poor people in Shanghai has increased sharply last year. Half of them are due to the lack of work, and most of them are from places where there is starvation." This also shows that the living conditions of the people in our country are more difficult than in the past.

The organization of the unemployed hunger brigade clearly indicates the extreme plight of the general population. The power of this group is strong. If the authorities do not have adequate relief measures, the peace of society may not be maintained. The right to eat is something that everyone should have. But in today's world, there is a large group of people who are trapped on the hunger line, unable to survive and unable to live. How dangerous is this phenomenon?

The Last Lesson 208

— Ling Bing

"Teacher, don't teach from the book..."

"Talk about current events, teacher..."

When I stepped into the classroom, before I had even opened the civics textbook, more than thirty children were chattering like a flock of sparrows. I pretended to be stern, slammed my right hand heavily on the podium, and shouted:

"Don't make noise;"

The children immediately quieted down, and countless dark eyes kept rolling at me, apparently eagerly waiting for me to talk about current events.

"Today we will teach from the book... The books for this semester haven't been taught..."

The classroom boiled again like a rolling pot, and dozens of small mouths stubbornly sent out a unified request: "Talk about current events, teacher!" When a child silently opened the cover of his desk and took out a civics textbook and spread it out in front of him, the eyes of everyone around him were all directed at him, and many mouths even made a hissing sound, forcing him to blush and stuff the textbook back in its place.

I chuckled, but this laugh was more painful than crying.

"Then I'll tell you some interesting stories."

"No, teacher. We want to hear about current events!"

I stood helplessly behind the podium, coughing dryly, unable to say a word.

Because of the children's fervent request, I talked to them about current events several times based on newspaper materials. Unexpectedly, I was severely warned by the principal because of this. He said that someone outside the school was saying that I was always promoting something in the classroom, and he sincerely asked me not to talk about current events anymore, for the sake of the school and for his position. I nodded, smiled wryly, and didn't say a word. I fabricated a few interesting stories in painful remorse, preparing to use these stories to replace current events when necessary. But the current facts prove that my hard work to deceive the children was in vain. What else can I say?

"Mr. Huang, you're really too much, letting them fool around like this." The principal suddenly stepped into the classroom, raised his eyebrows and said to me. He then turned his body half a circle, straightened his face, and shouted at the children:

"Is this civics class or current events class? Alas!... If Mr. Huang is polite, you can fool around lawlessly? Take out your textbooks quickly."

A small commotion immediately arose in the classroom. Amidst the crackling sound of desks opening and closing and the rustling sound of turning pages, there was also a vague roar, which caused the principal's anger to erupt again.

"Who said something?" Two pairs of eyes swept across the children's faces like lightning.

Grave-like silence. The principal glared at them angrily, and walked away silently.

I wanted to say something, but I couldn't say it. I only felt my lips trembling violently. I grabbed the book and glanced at the children in front of me. They were like a flock of pitiful lambs mechanically staring at the books in front of them under invisible pressure. Their tightly frowned brows showed a kind of helpless hidden pain of daring to be angry but not daring to speak out. My heart ached as if it were being pricked by countless needles.

I forced myself to finish reading a paragraph of the book. It was time to explain, but I couldn't explain it, as if something was tightly gripping my throat. For the price of a twenty-dollar monthly salary, I actually sold my soul, and I didn't hesitate to inject the innocent children's veins with poison that was more deadly than arsenic. Was this right?

I suddenly bit my teeth, threw the textbook on the table, and shouted loudly: "Everyone close your books and listen to me talk about current events!"

The children shuddered at the same time, raised their heads, and opened their surprised eyes, as if asking: "Have you gone crazy, teacher?"

"But I tell you: this is my last lesson." So I boldly and loudly talked about this week's current events...

The next morning, when I stepped out of the school gate with my luggage, a group of children came to surround me, asking me why I was leaving the school.

"Have you forgotten what I said yesterday? 'This is my last lesson.'" I answered with a wry smile.

Tong Zi Road 209

— Especially

I thought to myself: In this well-secured city, I can sleep soundly for one big night, right?

A heavy stone fell from my heart. Old Tie and I were staying in the back room on the east side. The wall was really white, without a single stain. It was telling the travelers that this inn was new and hadn't been ruined yet.

After finishing dinner, a refreshing cool breeze blew through the streets. Based on past experience, we realized that the weather at night would change. Never mind, the three of us walked on the central road. The shops, the displays, everything gave us a novel feeling.

Let's go in, A Huang pointed to a shop on the right: Let's listen to two sections of storytelling and then go back.

A Huang was very familiar with the situation in the mountain country. He knew what was produced there and how much it cost. The storytelling hall had a long room with many canvas deck chairs lined up on both sides. In the middle, there was also a not-very-handy tea table. A narrow aisle was left in the center of the room, and an oil lamp hung from the top of the aisle. Besides these, there were only the storytelling stage at the other end and a few couplets on the wall panels.

Perhaps it was too early. Except for us, I didn't

Page 20

see a fourth customer. It was strangely desolate. The old waiter with a mouthful of yellow teeth looked at us a few times with strange eyes. Maybe there were other languages in his eyes. Who knows? Waiting, waiting, half an hour slipped by. Rain, patter, fell. The storytelling stage was still lonely. When would we be able to hear the storytelling? Unwilling to continue to wait, we faced the sudden wind and rain and walked back home.

When it was almost time to sleep, the old servant came to this side with a wind lantern. Rainwater hung on his white beard, and his eyes, which had lost their luster, looked at everyone, panting. Without saying anything, we could know that there was a kind of hope in him.

—I said, Mr. Huang, he didn't dare to say it directly, smiled, shall I take the car tomorrow too?

—Taking the car costs five silver dollars. Old Huang also laughed.

No matter from which aspect, we had no reason to object, especially since the whole car was chartered! The old servant hurriedly left. Night swallowed up the entire space, and the earth was silent.

From Tongzi to Zunyi, this distance is not very far. It is estimated to be only about one hundred and twenty or thirty miles. If the speed of the long-distance bus is faster, then it will only take three hours to arrive.

Facing the dim face of dawn, we carried the items we needed to the company's bus station. The so-called bus station did not have a platform. It was only in our imagination that the buses in the mountain country were in a dilapidated state. However, the bus finally met us. The brand was Ford, and although the style was not very new, it was still passable. If you want to compare it, it is somewhat like the Shanghai-Minhang long-distance bus.

The driver was very young. He could speak the Shanghai dialect, fluent Mandarin, and also understood Cantonese slang. Really, distant travelers will feel closer to people from their hometown than to their own relatives. Our conversation was very speculative, and we opened up the unfamiliar wooden wall. He told us about the length of time he had worked here and the situation, the dynamics of this society and the local customs; talking, talking, without letting hypocrisy stay at all. I don't know how, the topic turned to future prospects. His face sank, he shook his head, and sighed deeply twice.

This gave us a hint that life in the mountain country was not easy after all!

The old servant hurried over. In addition to the cane, he also had a kerosene iron box. He put these two treasures on the bus, and also helped to tie them up and arrange them. The small pieces were placed in the car, and the long pieces were tied on the roof and sides of the car.

The car rushed out of the city amidst the crowd's watching, like a fierce tiger, rushing up the endless highway.

Under the Lamp 210

— Ma Jun

Jumping out of the rickshaw and paying the fare, he hurriedly escaped into the alley as if escaping from a demon. When he stopped in front of his door, he took out the key to open the door and went in without even ringing the doorbell. Stepping into the living room, the clock had just struck nine, and he finally breathed a sigh of relief. He took a cigarette from the tobacco jar on the table, lit it with a lighter, and ran upstairs. He met his wife coming out of the telephone room on the half-stairway, but she went upstairs to her room as if she hadn't seen him. So he rushed up in one stride, shouting:

"Hurry up, it's already nine o'clock."

His wife had a tight face and was already sitting on the sofa. Seeing this situation, he slowed down his pace at the doorway, slowly walked to his wife's side, and gently patted his wife's shoulder like every good husband, saying, "Isn't there still time? What are you angry about?"

His wife pursed her lips at him and turned her face in the opposite direction from her husband, as if talking to herself: "Leaving the office at six o'clock and not coming back until this time."

Understanding this, the husband shrugged his shoulders lightly, sat on the armrest of the sofa, and deliberately slickly faced his wife's face, saying in a low voice:

"Let's go see the play first, I'll tell you about the company's business later." He grabbed his wife's arm and wanted to pull her up, but his wife angrily shook his hand away, threw her body to the other corner of the sofa, and stared out the window. Outside the window was a dark sky without a moon.

The husband stood up, threw the cigarette butt out the window, and rubbed his hands, like when he encountered difficult situations in the company. He walked around the table in circles, his leather shoes squeaking, but he couldn't bear to explain to his wife the reason for coming back late in the simplest words. The stammering things almost confused his mind. "What do you women know?" He couldn't help but blurt out.

His wife immediately turned over from the corner of the sofa, repeating his words, "What do you women know? Women don't understand these things anyway. Leaving the office at six o'clock and not coming back until nine——o'clock." She dragged the end of the sound out long and made people uncomfortable.

"Okay, I was wrong." The husband still walked gently to his wife's side, "Let's go, it's about to start, this is the last show."

"I don't want to watch!" His wife turned her head to stare out the window again, "Today is like tomorrow, and tomorrow is like today. What exactly are you busy with? When I call the company, I can't find your shadow at all. Humph, you think I don't know..."

"Yin, what are you talking about?" The husband just raised his voice, but immediately lowered it again: "Didn't I tell you? My business is not just sitting in the office. So many things need me to arrange."

"I just don't know what these..." His wife's throat raised instead, "I have never heard of a manager running around the streets like a street vendor!"

The husband waved his hand, feeling like there was no reason to understand? He sat on the chair in front of the window, casually dragged the newspaper of the day and flipped through it, completely forgetting about watching the movie, and not paying attention to his wife's actions. His mind was spinning with that deal again: the telegram that the ship in Changsha had not set sail, while the Hakka in Shanghai urged the ship to leave, but he couldn't let go of this sale. It would be a small loss if his ship came back without goods, and he couldn't let other companies easily pull away his account in such a declining market. He discussed this matter with the Hakka this afternoon, and he asked the Hakka to wait until tonight. If there was no telegram from Changsha again, he would have no way to hold on to this account. But he also remembered that his wife wanted to watch that movie, and today was the last show. At half past eight, he left the restaurant where he was treating the Hakka to dinner, hurried to the company and ordered the night staff to call his home as soon as they received the telegram, and then hurried home by car, but what do women know: Thinking, he threw the newspaper and habitually rubbed his hands again.

His wife didn't expect her husband to be so indifferent to her, and she was even more certain that her guess was not wrong. Her husband loved her, but lately her husband hadn't come home early for a single day. That movie had been showing for a week, but it was always tomorrow, like tomorrow, and when she called the company, she couldn't find anyone. She was sure that her husband had changed his mind, and she buried her head and cried sadly.

At this time, the bell in the telephone room rang. The husband was worried about the telegram and immediately jumped out of the room, but his wife rushed down the stairs ahead of him. The husband stood at the doorway, pricking up his ears to listen to the sounds below. What he hoped for was the telegram from Changsha, but he couldn't hear what his wife was saying in the telephone room. After a while, he saw his wife walking upstairs, turning past him, and saying as if to another person: "The telegram from Changsha has arrived. The Hakka is waiting for you at the company to discuss."

The husband immediately wanted to run downstairs, but he went back into the room again, walked behind his wife, and gently stroked her shoulder, saying: "Isn't that right? Those things are enough to keep people busy! I'll get it done today and take you to see a movie tomorrow."

"Go on." His wife let go of his body and asked, "What are you doing tomorrow?"

His wife's smiling face was reflected again under the silver light.

A Toss 211

— Ji Nan

The early summer breeze brushed across people's faces. At dusk, Avenue Joffre was filled with a romantic atmosphere. Under the shimmering neon lights, the red lips, dark circles, and long eyelashes of enchanting women floated by. A young man pursed his lips and whistled a tune popular in the dance halls, matching it with his footsteps, passing by sweetly, passionately, joyfully, and lightly. Dusk is the beginning of the day in the metropolis.

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

I skillfully maneuvered through the crowd, a sea of people. There were glamorous noblewomen and peaceful night gentlemen, and an old man with eight-hundred-degree nearsighted glasses, hurriedly recording the results of a game. A Filipino with a sideways cap, his hands thrust into his trouser pockets, paced back and forth impatiently. The fervent atmosphere and the clamorous voices made me feel anxiously hungry.

The heroes on the court—toys of fate—were active again, flashes of red clothing, flashes of green clothing, flashes of clothing of various colors. The ball flew with these flashes of red and green, making rhythmic sounds, striking again and again at the tense heartstrings of the gamblers, shattering the hopes of many. Although occasionally it struck the hearts of some who were waiting, causing them to emit a joyful smile. The referee's whistle was like the verdict of a judge. In a single whistle, the hopes of many were destroyed; in a single whistle, the fate of many was pronounced. Hope hung in the corners of everyone's eyes, and this hope permeated golden dreams. Life would leap with the flashes of red and green, and fate was being hammered by the sound of the ball.

Although it was already midnight, the people in the stadium had long lost their sense of time. The atmosphere was exceptionally fervent, and the voices were even more clamorous. I transferred the last two one-yuan banknotes from my right hand to my left, and then casually grabbed a handful of copper coins from my pocket, the money I had prepared for the ride home, to count them, to decide this last destiny.

One, two, three... thirteen. Thirteen is an unlucky number! I'd better buy number two! I angrily threw the last two banknotes onto the ticket counter and exchanged them for a number two ticket.

Hope was very渺茫. I seemed to know that these last two yuan would not bloom into beautiful flowers. However, before knowing the result, no one could say that all hope was lost. I deliberately turned my head back, wanting to forget that there was still a glimmer of hope, and prepared to be indifferent, when suddenly I heard the joyful announcement of number two's victory.

Flashes of red clothing, flashes of green clothing, flashes of clothing of various colors. The ball flew with these flashes of red and green. Number two and number three each scored four points, creating the most tense situation. A trembling heart could not stop it from leaping with the flight of the ball. I subconsciously squeezed the ticket in my hand tightly into a long, thin strip. Everyone held their breath, waiting for the fate to come. A few minutes later, a whistle ended this tense scene. Everyone's fate followed, like the buzzing of ten thousand flies trapped in a cage, unable to fly. Everything was boiling over, and everything that was dead was revived. Like a pair of defeated roosters, I staggered out of the stadium.

Stepping on the midnight pavement, there was a bit of desolate meaning. Looking at the distant streetlights, it was like having a dream. I hoped to see the sun of the next day immediately.

Storytelling with Stringed Instruments 213

He Yunfang and He Qinfang's Double Pearl Phoenix

Sino-Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Chai Tou Feng"

Passionate love is always foolish. Ill-fated beauties have been spoken of since ancient times. I, Xianxian, lost my parents at a young age and had no one to rely on. I was raised as a lonely adopted daughter until I reached adulthood. The engagement with my cousin was originally a matter of righteousness. The whole family happily spent their days. What was even more pleasing was that my cousin's affection was also deep. He whispered sweet words of tenderness. Only to hate, the greedy Buddhist nun not being successful in begging. Only to regret. I politely declined, thus forming a deep hatred. The Chai Tou Feng, broken and fallen, was it intentional? It stirred up an extraordinary disaster. The manipulation was nothing more than revenge. The Buddhist nun should be killed. Vile words accused my mother of harming me. I bore countless hardships and grievances. My aunt's anger did not subside and changed even more. She actually made me live alone in a Buddhist temple, suffering abuse. The evil nun would entice me to vile deeds. I vowed to uphold my chastity and would not comply. My husband knew nothing and went far away to take the exam. Ten thousand kinds of sorrows, to whom could I express them? Langli returned and was fortunate to meet me. I was even more sad, recalling the lotus blossoms on the same stalk, difficult to achieve. Alas, I am endowed with a heart-rending tale that I cannot bear to read. Alas, my tears fall drop by drop, warming my silk handkerchief. Alas, I think about the past and the future, difficult to dream. Alas, I toss and turn all night, sleepless. Alas, I fear to face the mirror with my haggard face. Alas, I am entangled in bed, truly sick. Alas, may Kun Peng continue to remind me. Alas, I revive from death, my mother-in-law calling me. I cannot greet her morning and evening. I wish to at least unfold my brow. I must forgive my unfilial name. I sigh that my karmic fate was determined in a previous life. Why must I resent others for the torment? I only hope that heaven knows my intention. The gatherings and separations in life are like floating duckweed. I will willingly close my eyes and go to the underworld.

Xu Wenbi's Opening

Aviation (1180) 11:15 AM to 12:00 PM

Opening "Dai Yu Asks About Her Illness"

The vast blue sky gradually fades into dusk. A rustling breeze and fine rain sprinkle down. The dim Dai Yu's voice is silent. The desolate, slender bamboo casts a deep shadow. The affectionate Jia Baoyu cares deeply. He is worried about the sentimental and sickly woman. He hastily gets dressed and puts on his belt. Holding a lamp, he hurriedly walks to the garden. He has already arrived at the Xiang Pavilion. The young lady is, composing poetry, putting down her pen. The maid suddenly reports that the second master is here. She sees that his attire today is different from usual. Wide and loose, what is the matter, why emulate the fisherman's form? Baoyu, hearing this, hurriedly asks. Sister, are you at peace? Can you take medicine, can you eat more rice? Recently, you must not recite poetry. I am always worried, so I brave the rain to see you. Sister, you cannot bear this attire. I will send you a set on a later date. Daiyu replies, why do you need this? The image of a fisherman is truly meaningless. As the words leave her mouth. She silently thinks. Fishermen and fisherwomen should not be spoken of. Her peach blossom face flushes with a hard-to-hide blush. She silently lowers her head and says nothing. One is, unintentionally speaking wrongly, the other is, not hearing the truth, how would she know the affection, The Dream of the Red Chamber is full of transformations. I'll briefly mention that, Asking About the Illness, a section of the love story between Daiyu and Baoyu. I hate that the old matchmaker does not tie the threads of love. Hence, the medicine is useless, bearing two hearts.

Movie News

"Prisoner of Shark Island" Opens 215

Elected as one of the world's top ten blockbusters of the year

The historical and artistic epic "Prisoner of Shark Island," produced by 20th Century Fox with all its strength, is scheduled to premiere at the Grand Theater tonight (Wednesday) at 9:15 PM. The film tells the story of a noble doctor who is wrongly imprisoned for the assassination of Lincoln. Trapped on a remote island, far from his beloved wife and daughter, he endures an inhuman life. Relentless bullets, man-eating sharks, raging waves, and vicious demons all attack him. The plot is sorrowful and tense, enough to stand shoulder to shoulder with So-Oh's "Tears of the Stars" and Dumas' "The Count of Monte Cristo." Warner's performance in this film is also his greatest success ever. This is indeed a fine film that is capable of making everyone shed tears.

"These Three" to be Released 216

Starring Merle Oberon and Miriam Hopkins

United Artists' latest production, the artistic and tragic film "These Three," is a successful film in every aspect. Goldwyn's production, Hellman's script, William Wyler's direction, and the acting of Merle Oberon (the star of "The Dark Angel"), Miriam Hopkins (the star of "Vanity Fair"), and others are simply all successful. There are also child stars Bonita Granville and Marcia Mae Jones, who have even more unexpected success. Indeed, they are the discovered little stars of the year. The story is adapted from the famous Broadway stage play "The Children's Hour," which is very stimulating and moving. Merle and Miriam share a doctor, which leads to many disputes, and the future of the three is ruined. The film is scheduled to be released at the International Theater starting on Friday.
